The Paris Talks Come to an End

Britain, France, and the United States Achieve Solid Progress in Adjusting Views; Italy Also Has No Objections; Arms Supervision Will Be Trialed for Four Years 17

(Paris) As a result of the talks among the British, French, and American disarmament representatives, France and Britain have tentatively agreed to support the US President's new four-year trial method for supervising armaments. The idea of ​​supervising armaments was originally proposed by Britain, and France developed it into a detailed plan, advocating the organization of an impartial international committee to implement supervision. Each committee member would be able to go to the signatory countries to inspect armed forces and munitions factories. This agreement was intended to last for ten years. The French representative stated at the last Disarmament Conference that France could not join any disarmament agreement that did not include provisions for supervising armaments, which shows the French side's firm attitude. However, the US President believes that the ten-year period is too long, advocating for a shorter period so that if the countries concerned find it unsatisfactory, it can be modified from time to time. Therefore, there is a proposal for a four-year trial. As for the detailed methods, the US President has not yet announced them. It is expected that the US representative Davis will announce them in detail after the Disarmament Conference reopens on October 16. As for Italy, although it did not participate in the talks here, it is heard that the Italian representative has received instructions to approve this plan. (22nd National Telegram)

Germany Accepts with Conditions 18

(Paris) The German Ambassador to Paris visited British Ambassador Duler this morning. Although political circles are silent about the German ambassador's visit, it is expected that the ambassador personally conveyed Germany's answer regarding disarmament to Ambassador Duler. According to the Paris Echo, Germany is willing to accept supervision, but it must be allowed to build defensive works on the western border like those built by France, and it must be allowed to place heavy artillery. Bombing aircraft should be discarded, but chase aircraft should be retained, and Germany should be allowed to place them. Furthermore, international management should be conducted after the signing of each treaty. (Reuter's dispatch)

Many Thorns Ahead 19

(Paris) Britain and France continued talks today on the disarmament convention, first at a banquet at the British Embassy and then at the French Foreign Ministry. The British representatives were Foreign Secretary Simon, Under-Secretary Eden, and Head of the League of Nations Diplomatic Division, who has recently been appointed as Minister to China, Kedu Gan. The French representatives were President Daladier, Foreign Minister Pangou, and Massigli. British Privy Council President Baldwin was also present at the British Embassy banquet but did not join the discussions after the banquet. The most difficult problem that needs to be resolved urgently is the length of the trial period. MacDonald's plan only stipulates that offensive armaments should be destroyed within nine months from the date of implementation of the treaty. It is heard that the British government is unwilling to accept the French theory of fixed-term and automatic management, but if it is revised and France supports the British draft of March 16, then Britain may also accept the French proposal. The discussion at the French Foreign Ministry lasted for one and a half hours and invited Davis, the US representative to the Disarmament Conference, to the ministry to listen to the progress made in the British-French talks. As for how things are progressing, British and French cabinet members are unwilling to reveal it to the press. Only the communique stated that the purpose of the exchange of views between the two sides was to reach an understanding so that all debates at the Disarmament Conference, which will reopen next month, could proceed smoothly, and that the two sides had made solid progress in this regard. Simon is scheduled to go to Geneva tonight, and Davis and Pangou are scheduled to go tomorrow. The French cabinet will also hold a meeting tomorrow. According to reliable sources, in today's discussion, Britain, France, and Italy have reached solid progress in adjusting their views on this matter. It is heard that the general opinion is that the disarmament convention should be divided into two stages: (1) three or four years (a static period), during which Germany will replace long-term service troops with short-term service troops; (2) a real disarmament stage, implemented in three or four years. Although the principle of supervision has been generally recognized, the three countries still have different opinions on the method of implementation. Britain believes that reporting the number of armaments is more important than just discussing any supervision of armaments that does not specify the number. However, if the convention can be finalized, the amount of armaments that France is prepared to give up will also be deeply reassuring to Britain. As for the current naval treaty, it will not be changed before it expires. Although things have made good progress, there are still many thorns ahead, and it is not yet possible to be overly optimistic. (23rd Reuter's dispatch)

Report to Respective Governments 20

(Paris) Today, representatives from Britain, France, and the United States met. According to the communique, the talks today have yielded important results. These talks will be temporarily suspended so that each representative can report the progress of the talks to their respective governments. How to handle the discussion of each issue will be decided by each government. The French side will hold a cabinet meeting at the Rambouillet Palace tomorrow. It is probably necessary to wait for Britain and the United States to express their approval of the measures decided today before the French side can express a definite opinion. In addition to waiting for the approval of their respective governments, the opinions of all parties were very close at today's meeting. The French point of view has been generally approved by the British representatives. As for the contact with the Italian government, it is handled by the embassy in Rome. According to official telegrams, Italy's opinions are also close to those of Britain and France. Now, only the approval of the United States is awaited. Davis said that he has agreed to the opinions of Britain and France, but he is waiting for the approval of the White House. This meeting was a useful preparation for the reopening of the Disarmament Conference. The Italian representative to the Disarmament Conference, Aleazzi, will hold negotiations with Germany. This is undoubtedly the most difficult step before concluding a disarmament convention. However, since the major countries have reached an agreement, it is not difficult to take a common front against Germany. (22nd Havas dispatch)

French Foreign Ministry Communique 21

(Paris) At 7:00 PM today, after the conclusion of the talks between the representatives of Britain, the United States, and France on the Disarmament Conference, the Foreign Ministry issued a communique stating, "As a result of repeated talks, the viewpoints of the three governments have become clearer. Last time, the US representative Davis, the British representative Eden, and the representatives of the French government gave a general explanation of the opinions of their respective governments. Now they are reiterating them. The purpose of this work is to prepare for the Disarmament Conference so that it can proceed smoothly. The progress made is still quite rich," and so on. (22nd Havas dispatch)

(London) The well-known political writer Major General Morgan revealed a letter in The Times today, explaining the difficulty of supervising armaments, saying that the British plan to manage armaments by implementing it with a delegation of commissioners dispatched by the League of Nations is actually difficult to implement. Those who have not served on this kind of commission do not know the difficulty of investigating the truth. This kind of management, with unprepared investigations as an indispensable element, and this kind of sudden investigation, is similar to a police random search, which often makes people unhappy. The League of Nations Administrative Council Approves Technical Cooperation with China; Gu Weijun Declares No Political Nature 23

(Geneva) The Administrative Council of the League of Nations held another meeting this morning, which lasted quite a short time and was still chaired by Norwegian representative Mowinkel. The Administrative Council first listened to the report of Spanish representative Madariaga on the current situation of international public works issues, and then approved the resolution of the Technical Cooperation Committee. Previously, the Chinese government had requested the League of Nations to cooperate technically with the Economic Committee of the Chinese Government. The League of Nations organized a committee to pass the conditions for technical cooperation between the two parties and agreed to appoint Dr. Rajchman, the director of the Health Division of the Secretariat of the League of Nations, as the liaison officer between the League of Nations and the Economic Conference of the Chinese Government. The committee's report had clearly pointed this out. (23rd Havas dispatch)

US-Russian Diplomatic Recognition Under Consideration in the White House 24

Hull Prepares a Report for Presidential Review

Cotton Promotion Market is a Major Motivation

(Washington) Regarding the issue of the United States formally recognizing the Soviet Union, the authorities are already considering it. According to reliable sources, it is speculated that when Congress reopens in November, the government will submit the recognition as a fait accompli to Congress.

Also, it is reported that the current dissatisfaction of the American cotton industry with the status quo is a major motivation for the United States to recognize Soviet Russia, because if the United States recognizes Soviet Russia, the Russian side can purchase American cotton. (23rd Reuter's dispatch)

The issue of recognizing Soviet Russia is included in the report. Hull advocates conditional recognition of Soviet Russia, that is, the rights of the American people to the demands that can be made to Soviet Russia must be guaranteed. Former US Ambassador to Turkey, Morgenthau, is currently in New York, negotiating with the Soviet Russian trade representative, planning to have the United States pay 50 million yuan in advances to Soviet Russia so that it can purchase American cotton. From San Diego to Honolulu

Route is Over Two Thousand Nautical Miles Long

Bahia Honda (Panama Canal) The US Navy plans to conduct a formation flight between San Diego and Honolulu this winter. However, this time there were only six aircraft, but in the future there will be twelve. This route is 2,500 miles long, with more places to dock along the way, so it is less dangerous. Hirota Praises Economic Cooperation Between Japan and the United States 29

(Tokyo) The new Foreign Minister, who is in charge of diplomacy in the emergency situation, delivered a speech at the Foreign Ministry garden using the American Fox Corporation's broadcasting equipment yesterday afternoon on the 22nd, as follows: (The United States is exercising the Industrial Recovery Act and seeking countermeasures for large-scale plans in order to open up the economic panic. Japan Expands the Authority of the Chief of the Naval General Staff 30

The Theory of Civilians Appointing Naval Ministers is Eliminated

(Tokyo) The revision of the Naval General Staff Act will be submitted to the Emperor by Naval Minister Osumi on the 25th and 26th, and will be promulgated on the same day after being approved by the Emperor. The focus of the revision is Article 3 of the Naval General Staff Regulations, which states (The Chief of the Naval General Staff participates in matters of national defense and the use of troops, and after review, transfers it to the Minister of the Navy. However, in wartime, when there is no general headquarters, the Chief of the Naval General Staff conveys matters regarding operations). Part of the article has been revised, expanding the command authority of the Chief of the Naval General Staff, regardless of peacetime or wartime. At the same time, there is no doubt that as a result of the revision, the authority of the Minister of the Navy and the Chief of the Naval General Staff regarding the determination of military and political forces determined in July of the Showa 5th year has become more clear. Command matters are initiated by the Chief of the Naval General Staff and consulted with the Minister of the Navy, and military and political matters are initiated by the Minister of the Navy and consulted with the Chief of the Naval General Staff. Therefore, the issue of interfering with the command authority that was provoked at the London Conference is no longer in danger of recurring. At the same time, due to the relationship of the Military Advisory Conference, it is an absolute requirement to appoint an official to serve as the Minister of the Navy. The theory of using civilians has naturally been eliminated. (23rd Telecommunications Agency dispatch)

Britain Holds Autumn Exercises 31

German Military Attaché Invited to Participate

This is the First Time After the European War

(London) The German military attaché at the German Embassy in London has received an invitation from the British military authorities to participate in the autumn maneuvers held by the British in Salisbury this year. This is the first time that a German military attaché has been invited to participate after the European War. Other countries such as Italy, the United States, France, Japan, Soviet Russia, and Spain have also been invited to send representatives to participate. (22nd National Telegram)

Deterioration of False Relationship Between Russia and False State: Russian Consulate in Harbin Denies Searching False Vessel 32

Rejects Three Demands and Accuses False State of Sheltering White Russian Activities

(Harbin) The relationship between Russia (Manchuria) has become even more serious since the exchange of letters between the representatives of both sides stationed in Harbin. The Russian Consul-General in this area, Slavsky, responded to Shi Luben, the (Manchurian) diplomatic negotiator, stating that the (Manchurian) side claimed that in July of this year, Soviet Russian political secret detectives searched the (Manchurian) ship "Dongshan" in (Manchurian) territorial waters. This statement is completely unfounded. He also stated that the three conditions proposed by Shi, (1) the release of the White Russian guards arrested on the "Dongshan" vessel, (2) severely punish the personnel of the Soviet Russian Secret Detective Bureau involved in this case, (3) guarantee that the same incident will not occur again in the future, (4) the Russian side cannot accept or acknowledge any of them, and can only forward them to the Soviet Russian government for its information. The Russian Consul-General later expressed dissatisfaction in his reply note, stating that the (Manchurian) authorities allowed White Russians to infiltrate Russian territory, and that the (Manchurian) side did not take any steps to suppress the White Party leader General Kong Shiming, and other White Party organizations dispatching hostile troops into Russia, which has led to a further deterioration in relations between the two countries. Shi Luben immediately replied to the Russian Consul-General's note, stating that the Russian side should pay attention to the fundamental facts of the case, which cannot be denied by any official explanation. The document also mentioned that when the "Dongshan" vessel was searched, it was within the territorial waters of (Manchukuo), and accused the Soviet Russian Consul-General's explanation of obscuring the facts. As for the Russian note's accusation that the (Manchurian) side does not interfere with White Russian activities, Shi stated that it was a trick by the Russian Consul-General to shift the focus of the dispute. Finally, he stated that the Soviet Russian authorities should immediately accept and implement the three conditions proposed by the (Manchurian) side. (Reuter's telegram on the 23rd)

French Parliamentary Delegation Goes to Italy for On-the-Spot Investigation 37

Paris, National News, 22nd A delegation of forty members of the French Senate and Chamber of Deputies set off for Rome today to conduct an on-the-spot investigation of Italy's economic issues. After meeting Italian Prime Minister Mussolini in Rome tomorrow, they will be accompanied by the reception committee chaired by Italian Finance Minister Reng to tour the Italian capital for two days, and then take a special train to Naples, Florence, Venice, Milan, Turin, and other cities to inspect factories, rural areas, and the wine industry. Although the departure of the parliamentary delegation today does not carry any mission from the government, it is reported that French Prime Minister Daladier has high hopes for it. Since the European War, Franco-Italian relations have been affected by nationalism in both diplomacy and economy, and there have been some estrangements. The visit of the parliamentary delegation to Italy is not only a sign of the new friendship between France and Italy after the Four-Power Pact, but also a prelude to improving economic relations. Because after the failure of the London Economic Conference, improving Franco-Italian economic relations is the most important and difficult issue for the Daladier government. Although the parliamentarians do not have the power to negotiate and amend tariffs, Daladier really hopes that they can obtain sufficient records and return to the country, so as to lay the foundation for the two countries to eliminate existing barriers. Because this move must be supported by both houses of parliament, Daladier has high expectations for the trip of the parliamentarians. It is reported that the parliamentarians are scheduled to return to the country on October 6, and Parliament will open a week later.

Chen Qúzhēn Resolves the Remnants of Chén and Yán's Forces 63

Chén Wò and Yán Zhòngrú Retreat to the Guizhou Border

Chén Qúzhēn Cables Hé Jiàn with News of Victory

Changsha Correspondence: Hé Jiàn's former subordinates, Brigade Commander Chén Wò and Division Commander Yán Zhòngrú, were dismissed from their posts last year due to various reasons, and their troops were reorganized and disbanded. After being relieved of their commands, Chén and Yán harbored resentment and, in May of this year, colluded with miscellaneous troops in western Hunan, occupying Zhījiāng, Qiányáng, and Huàng counties. They raised the banner of rebellion against Hé, issuing a public telegram listing various accusations against Hé Jiàn. Hé Jiàn then mobilized Chén Qúzhēn's division and the two brigades of Lǐ Guójūn and Chén Zǐxián, launching a large-scale offensive. Because miscellaneous troops in western Hunan and bandits such as Yáo Jìyú, Zhōu Yùchéng, and Liào Xiāngyún (former commander of the Hǔmén Fortress) responded to Chén Wò, the anti-Hé forces became quite strong. Therefore, after three or four months of siege by the Hé army, Zhījiāng County was finally captured on August 25th. Chén, Yán, and their troops, numbering about three or four regiments, retreated to the area around Xióngshān on the border of Zhījiāng, Máyáng, and Lúxī. Hé Jiàn again telegraphed Chén Qúzhēn's troops to be responsible for the pursuit and ordered the two brigades of Lǐ Guójūn and Chén Zǐxián to handle the aftermath in the Zhījiāng, Qián, and Huàng area. Chén Qúzhēn then dispatched the brigade of Lǐ Kědá and the regiment of Liú Wénzhāng from his command, starting on September 9th, to pursue in separate routes until the 16th, when the situation was resolved. Chén and Yán both retreated to the border of Guizhou Province. The following is a report from Chén Qúzhēn: (Your subordinate has repeatedly telegraphed reports regarding the pursuit and suppression of the rebel troops of Chén and Yán. Recently, it was reported that the majority of the rebels had fled to Xióngshān on the border of Zhī, Má, and Lú, where they were stubbornly resisting. Subsequently, under the command of Regiment Commander Liú Wénzhāng, our troops launched a fierce attack. The rebels, due to insufficient food supplies, secretly moved from Xióngshān to Yánzhài, Héshuǐ, Sōngyú, and other places on a beautiful evening, attempting to flee back to Máyáng, Shàngshān, Gǎngshí, and secretly enter the Guizhou Province border to gather and cause trouble. Your subordinate ordered Regiment Commander Liú to pursue and also ordered Second Brigade Commander Tián Liúshǒushìyuán, stationed in Má, to supervise the military groups and deploy them at Wèngtǒng, Diàoyán, Tángjiāwān, and other places to intercept. The enemy's situation was extremely desperate. Later, they changed their route, fleeing through Liǎngxī Bābā'ào and secretly entering Zàonítán in Fèng county, planning to take the road through Xīncáng to enter Guizhou. Your subordinate also ordered First Brigade Commander Lǐ Kědá to send troops to lie in ambush near Huánghèyíng to intercept them. Unexpectedly, the rebel troops had already secretly arrived at Huánghèyíng and occupied Xīnzàiyíng and Ānjìng Guān. Just as Regiment Commander Liú and his military groups had arrived in pursuit, they launched a joint attack on the rebel troops at dawn on a cold day, engaging in a fierce battle until 3 PM, killing many rebels. The remaining rebels, due to running out of ammunition, voluntarily surrendered their weapons and were sent away. In this battle, a total of over seven hundred and fifty rifles and carbines were seized, with only one or two rows of bullets per gun. According to the prisoners, after leaving Xióngshān, Yán had fled alone to Shěng Huàng, where the provinces of Hunan and Guizhou meet. Chén, after fleeing to Tiānqípíng, mingled with Zhōu Yùchéng's bandit troops and secretly returned to Zhōu's fortress in Bàoxī. After distributing the seized weapons to the various regiments for use and sending away the rebel officers and soldiers, after thoroughly investigating and detaining them, in summary, your subordinate was ordered to supervise the suppression and has successively seized over eight hundred and forty rebel rifles. Currently, there are no traces of the rebels within the four borders of your subordinate's defense zone. The matter of how to compensate the wounded and killed personnel and reward the deserving officers and soldiers should be reasonably reported by telegram. I humbly request your review and instructions for compliance. Respectfully submitted by your subordinate Chén Qúzhēn, sealed) (September 18)

Russian Troops Gather Along the Siberian Railway, Actively Preparing for War Against Japan 64

Russian Troops Fill the Opposite Bank of the Great Black River　　Fortified Bunkers Built on Important Bridges　　Military Farming Communities Established in Garrison Areas　　Air Bases Constructed in Vladivostok and Other Places　　Harbin Correspondence: Soviet Russia has recently been strengthening its military preparations in the Primorsky Krai. The sale of the Eastern Railway is unlikely to be realized for the time being. However, it is actively preparing for war against Japan and its puppet state. The opposite bank of the Great Black River is filled with Red Army soldiers. Fortified bunkers have been built near important bridges on the Amur Railway to defend against air raids. A special winter fuel mobilization for 1933 has been ordered along the Trans-Baikal and Ussuri lines. Military farming communities have been established in garrison areas in the Far East. The Soviet Union's most potent weapon is its air force. Once war breaks out between Japan and Russia, Russian aircraft could easily fly to Japanese territory and bomb it. The details are listed below:

Double Tracks Between Omsk and Irkutsk 65

Before the Russian Revolution of 1917, the Siberian Railway had double tracks. However, in the years following the revolution, one track was dismantled, and all transportation relied on a single track. Now, the double tracks between Omsk and Irkutsk (the section from western Siberia to the west bank of Lake Baikal) have been laid. The sleepers on that section have been replaced, and the ballast has been laid. However, the rolling stock is in poor condition, and delays and derailments are common, causing damage to the locomotives. The main repair shop in Krasnoyarsk lacks skilled workers, and there is a shortage of parts and materials. The outdated equipment used for repairs is also an obstacle. In fact, the situation in all the repair shops along the line is similar. At major stations, damaged cars and locomotives are often parked, one after another. Some of these have the symbols of the Chinese Eastern Railway, and these cars are mostly used by the Red Army and are not allocated for commercial transport. Before the revolution, the Russian Far Eastern Railway could be divided into three sections: the Trans-Baikal section, connecting Irkutsk, Manzhouli, and Sretensk; the Amur section, leading to Khabarovsk; and the Ussuri section, connecting Khabarovsk and Vladivostok, with branch lines to Shuangcheng and Suifenhe. Currently, this division has changed. Between Irkutsk and Vladivostok, it is now divided into two sections: the Trans-Baikal and Ussuri railways, in addition to the former Amur section. The junction between these two lines is at Ruklov, the northernmost point on the Amur River (i.e., the Heilongjiang River), which is where the plane of the recent American global aviator Mattern was forced to land. The Trans-Baikal Railway is also divided into two sections. One runs along the shore of Lake Baikal and has double tracks. The other is a wartime track, a single track that goes directly to Vladivostok. However, to compensate, extra sidings have been built in several places to shorten the distance between major stations. In case of emergency, this would facilitate increased traffic. These sidings are built according to the tunnels, bridges, and terrain, spaced five, eight, or ten kilometers apart. Spacing of fifteen kilometers is rare.

Bunkers Built for Fuel 66

The bridges on the Amur Railway were mostly temporary wooden structures in the past, but now they have been almost completely replaced with reinforced concrete structures. Near the tunnels and important bridges, fortified bunkers have been built with flat roofs that can withstand air raids. Small squads of soldiers are stationed in the bunkers, carrying machine guns and anti-aircraft guns. Ditches and other obstacles have also been built. The Trans-Baikal and Ussuri lines have adequate fuel supplies, but the former Amur section is severely lacking in fuel. The coal used comes from the Jifu Dingski coal mine, and the quality is poor. To remedy this, the Soviet authorities have ordered a special winter fuel preparation mobilization for 1933.

Military Supplies Transported from European Russia 67

The Siberian Express runs only twice a week, and most of the transportation is for military supplies. Many goods are transported from European Russia, including various kinds of machinery. Recently, large quantities of pressed fodder for cavalry use have been transported. These items are labeled as supplies for collective farms. For example, military tanks are labeled as farm machinery. According to recent news, since March of this year, the Amur line has been managed by the Red Army. Political agents on the line are under the command of the Red Army's political department.

Airfields Built in Vladivostok 68

Since June or July of last year, the Amur Oblast has been undergoing large-scale military preparations. All activities along the road and in the towns are related to a practical military plan and are under military command. Since last year, efforts have been made to strengthen the defenses along the riverbank. This work is carried out by special engineering troops, engineers, and workers brought from European Russia, and guided by Germans in Red Army uniforms. No one is allowed to enter the area near these projects without permission, not even the local political agents. The Soviet Union is particularly focused on air defense in this region. Several airfields have been built between Ruklov and Khabarovsk. The airfield at Ruklov is particularly large, with maintenance areas, factories, and ammunition depots. The number of aircraft is unknown due to strict military secrecy. However, it is known that airfields have been built at the following locations: Bogarifu, Yakharara, Dikongkaiya, Boyakov, Khabarovsk, Spassk, Shuangchengzi, Vladivostok, Posyet, Yanuchino, Rasdolnoye, Su-zhuang, and Olga Bay. Air bases have also been built in the Okhotsk and Kamchatka regions. Although soldiers are not often seen in public places, air force personnel are frequently seen. They wear neat uniforms and enjoy special privileges, and their rations are supplied by special agencies, which other troops cannot access. It is said that their aviation skills are excellent and that they have all graduated from renowned aviation schools.

Military Farms Organized 69

Before the European War and the Russian Revolution, the Russian authorities, in order to wash away the shame of the Russo-Japanese War, stationed heavy troops in the Far East and built special forts. However, these facilities are now insufficient to accommodate the large number of Red Army troops. Therefore, the Soviet military authorities have established garrison areas, building barracks and residences suitable for both winter and summer. These garrison areas are separated from civilian residences by wide fences and electric fences. The families of officers and soldiers live in these areas. The Soviet Union once planned to organize military farming communities, providing them with good land and excellent tools. Currently, there are two military collective farms in the Amur Oblast, one in Tambovsky and one in Konstantinovsky.

Air Force Weapons Are Excellent 70

The strength of the Red Army should not be underestimated. Other countries' armies in the Far East will realize that they are not easy opponents once they engage with them. The Soviet Union's specialty is its air force. If war breaks out between Japan and Russia, Russian aircraft could easily fly to Japanese territory and bomb it. The defensive works are also very strong. The Red Army's weapons and equipment are excellent. There is a small type of tank that can accommodate two machine gunners and can travel thirty kilometers per hour on any type of road. The infantry uses automatic rifles, and there are new types of large and heavy artillery that can be transported by heavy trucks. Military training is also very thorough. The political espionage organization is a characteristic of the Red Army, ensuring that the soldiers are not discouraged. In short, the Red Army in the Far East today is preparing and eager to try its strength. (Northeast News Agency)

Over a Million People Massacred, Property Losses Amount to Tens of Millions of Yuan

New Record for Transportation Between Guangzhou and Shantou 75

Highway Through Transport Implemented, Telephone System Completed

Transportation between Shantou and Guangzhou has long relied on maritime transport, transiting through Hong Kong into the Pearl River. Foreigners controlled the maritime shipping business, and direct ships between Guangzhou and Shantou were scarce. Three years ago, only the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's Shanghai-Guangdong route had four or five ships per month passing through Shantou to Guangzhou. The journey was slow, taking twenty-six hours to arrive, and the docking at Bai'etan (White Swan Pool) made loading and unloading inconvenient. Therefore, most people traveling from Shantou to the provincial capital took the route through Hong Kong. In the last two years, the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company almost stopped running the Shanghai-Guangdong line, making it impossible to travel between Guangzhou and Shantou without going through Hong Kong. The Guangdong government, aware of the difficulties of sea transport between Guangzhou and Shantou, worked hard to build the first trunk line of the Eastern Provincial Highway. This line is two hundred miles long, starting from Haitoujiao Shiqu Wutian in Shantou, passing through Chaoyang Yuxia Sima Pu, entering Puning Liusha district, exiting Huilai Kuitan, turning to Lufeng Haifeng Pingshan, and ending at Tai'an Station on the Guangzhou-Kowloon Railway, connecting to the Guangzhou-Kowloon train to the provincial capital. This road was completed last winter, with only a few bridges yet to be finished. Previously, merchants had jointly funded a transportation company, and the Department of Construction had approved its operating franchise for a fixed number of years. However, each merchant operated independently on different sections, making transfers very difficult. Vehicles often failed to arrive at transfer points on time. Considering this, the provincial government, to facilitate transportation between the province and Shantou, decided to take back the three sections of the highway: Pu-Shan, Ping-Ren, and Hui-Ping, and operate them officially. On September 8th, Li Hua, the director of the Eastern Highway Bureau, was ordered to take over all vehicles and assets of the Ji Feng Company in the Pu-Shan section and set up an office in the Highway Bureau, with Li Hua concurrently serving as the general director. The office has three departments: General Affairs, Vehicle Affairs, and Engineering. Operations began on September 9th, with vehicles running as usual, and all income going to the government. According to Li Hua, an evaluation committee will soon be formed, with Chen Guoji appointed by the Department of Construction, Wang Yaochang by the Eastern District Public Office, and Wu Keqiang by the Highway Bureau. However, the First Army Group, the Municipal Government, the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, the Chaoyang Senate, and the Puning Senate have not yet appointed members. After the committee determines the price, the privately held shares will be repaid accordingly. It is also reported that the Ping-Ren and Hui-Ping sections are expected to be completely taken over this month. Before Double Ten Day (October 10th), through transport between Guangzhou and Shantou will be available. The Highway Bureau has purchased a large number of long-distance buses, which are being renovated. There are company-operated electric ferries from Shantou to Wutian across the sea and from Lei Shi to Houxi in Chaoyang across the sea. There is also a public ferry between Pingshan. There are eleven stations along the way. The journey starts from Shantou at 6:00 AM and arrives in the provincial capital at 7:30 PM. As for the ticket price, it needs to be determined in consultation with the Guangzhou-Kowloon Railway Bureau.

There were already wireless and wired telegraphs between Guangzhou and Shantou. In recent years, with local stability, their use has become quite convenient. This year, in June, a wireless telephone was installed, with the Shantou station located in Zhongshan Park. It has now been completely installed and the test results are good. It is scheduled to officially open on October 1st. The communication methods are: (A) Registration Method: (1) Households with automatic telephones can communicate at any time after paying a deposit. (2) Those without automatic telephones can bring their certificate to the station and communicate after paying a deposit. (3) Those who have not registered can also go to the station, pay the registration fee, and communicate immediately. The temporary registration fee will be refunded after the call is completed. (B) Types of Calls: (1) Regular calls: Can only be made to a specific number, not to a specific person. (2) Special calls: Can be made to a specific person. (3) Scheduled calls: Can be scheduled to communicate at a specific time every day. (4) Urgent calls: Can be made immediately, with instant connection. (C) Fee Schedule: For the first three minutes or less, regular calls cost three yuan, special calls cost three yuan and nine jiao, and scheduled calls are calculated as regular calls if scheduled more than fifteen days in advance. Urgent calls are charged double the rate. After the first three minutes, each additional minute or less costs one yuan for regular calls and one yuan and three jiao for special calls. Scheduled calls are charged an additional 30%. The above methods have been stipulated by the Department of Construction and issued to Shantou. The registration fee (i.e., registration of address) is twenty yuan per year and must be paid even for temporary calls, which will be refunded after the call. (September 15th)

Songjiang 76

Husband and Wife Commit Suicide by Poison

Xu Yuanqing, the owner of Xu Yichang Rice Shop in Kuatang Bridge, Songjiang, was known for his frugality and had accumulated considerable wealth. His third son, Xu Shunguan, married the daughter of Yang Yunquan, an eye doctor in the city. The couple felt harmonious, but Shunguan had been dissolute in the past, which his father disapproved of. In recent years, he had slightly reformed. He felt ashamed of his financial situation because his father had removed him from his sight. Last month, he was at a Le Ye Tea House listening to flower drum opera. Shunguan, encouraged by friends, ordered four plays. He did not pay for the plays at the time. Until the other day, the tea house owner went to the shop to demand payment. Shunguan took four silver dollars from the shop and paid. Yuanqing found out about this and was furious. He rebuked and ordered him to leave home, forbidding him from entering, to show his determination. Shunguan returned and told his wife. Because the couple's feelings were very deep, they did not want to be separated. So each secretly took sleeping pills and committed suicide together. His wife died first. Shunguan took a lighter dose and did not die. Now, Yang Yunquan's family has raised the matter. The local prosecutor's office also came to examine the body after receiving the report. The examination confirmed that they died from poison.

Continued Report on the Perilous Sea Dike 77

The dangerous situation of the sea dike in Jinshanwei, Punan, has been repeatedly reported in this newspaper. The most dangerous part is from Queerli to Qijia Dun, about seventeen li long. The stone foundation of the dike is exposed, and there is no slope. The tide rushes here violently, already directly impacting the base of the dike. If something unfortunate happens, the counties of Songjiang, Fengxian, and Jinshan may all become a watery land, and the loss of life and property would be incalculable. Yesterday, the county chamber of commerce, the property management office, and other organizations urgently telegraphed the provincial government for help, requesting the dispatch of personnel and allocation of funds for repairs as soon as possible. Commissioner Jin Tiqian has decided to hire a public bus at 7:00 AM tomorrow (the 23rd) to go directly to Jinshanwei for inspection, accompanied by Provincial Committee member Shen Zhengshu, county government technical director Xu Mojiia, secretary Wu Zhongyu, and guards. The findings of the inspection will be reported to the provincial government.

Flourishing Sales of Salt Permits in Songjiang Prefecture 78

Since Su's tax police were reorganized under the management of Songjiang Inspection Sub-bureau Director and Transport Deputy Song Zi'an, he has made great efforts to rectify the situation. The sales of salt permits in various places have increased significantly. According to recent surveys, the Fourth District under the bureau's jurisdiction has achieved the most notable results in patrolling. The sales of salt permits in various places in the entire district have been flourishing month by month this year. July's sales exceeded the target by more than 1,200 permits, and August's sales exceeded the target by more than 800 permits, totaling a surplus of more than 2,000 permits in two months.

Wuxi 79

Zhu Yunting Kidnapped and Escapes Dangerously

Zhu Yunting, a famous doctor in the second district of the county (Jingyun City), was kidnapped by four or five bandits at Yaohua Tan, about two li north of Gaochang'an in the sixth district, on the evening of the 15th of this month. Zhu's family repeatedly sent a family member, Zhou Afu, to contact the bandits. Because the ransom was too high, no agreement was reached. It is now known that after this case occurred, County Magistrate Yan Shenyu immediately ordered the chief of police, Wu Zhengrong, to conduct a thorough investigation and rescue the victim. After receiving the order, Chief Wu led the police in disguise to investigate in the area where the incident occurred and in the Yianqiao Zhangcun Temple area. After several days, there were clues to be found. The other night, Zhu Yunting took advantage of the fact that the guard was asleep and quietly escaped from the bandit's den and safely returned home. He described in detail the process of being kidnapped and the suffering he endured, sobbing as he spoke, tears streaming down his face, a tragic sight. It is also heard that Zhu was kidnapped by bandits once five years ago, losing more than 3,000 yuan before being able to return home. This is the second time he has been kidnapped, and his escape is a fortunate event.

Bailiff Accused of Fraud and Indecent Assault 80

Xu Xinren, a bailiff of the county court, is a relative of Xu Tiqian, the president of the court. He came to Wuxi with President Xu to serve. On the afternoon of July 11th of this year, Ren Yingbo and Ren Zhuqing, villagers of Dongxiang Township in the third district of the county, were involved in a lawsuit over a debt. The court sent Xu Xinren to the township to deliver a civil mediation summons. After Xu arrived in the township, he immediately summoned Zhang Huitian, the head of the twenty-fifth tu, and led him to Ren Zhuqing's house. Because Zhuqing was doing business in Shanghai, the summons was received by his relative, Ren Hesheng. Afterwards, Ren Hesheng alleged that Xu Xinren had demanded two silver dollars from him at the time and had indecently assaulted his daughter-in-law, Ren Qiu. Zhang Huitian, the head of the district, was also accused of assisting in the extortion and indecently assaulting his daughter, Guiying. Therefore, they filed a complaint with the county court's prosecutor's office. Yesterday, prosecutor Ren opened a court session to investigate. As a result, Xu Xinren and Zhang Huitian were both released on bail, and Ren Hesheng, Ren Qiu, and others were all ordered to return home.

Zhenjiang 81

Labor Dispute in the Thread-Making Industry

Li Jinyong, Ge Qiming, Yi Jinquan, and other workers in the Zhenjiang thread-making industry previously stated that the capital side (Jing Huo Shop) had suddenly announced to all workers on the first day of this month that if they wanted to continue working on thread, they would be paid 70% of the usual wage, otherwise, they could strike. Later, in order to avoid disputes, the labor side temporarily swallowed their anger and continued to work as usual. However, the labor and capital sides had regulations stipulating that neither side could unilaterally renege on the agreement. In addition, the workers' usual wages were not enough to live on, let alone if they were paid 70% of the usual wage. Therefore, they jointly submitted a petition to the Zhenjiang County Party Department yesterday, requesting the dispatch of personnel to mediate and ordering the capital side to pay the originally agreed-upon wage so that the workers' livelihoods could be maintained and to prevent a strike from occurring.

Gaoyou 82

Detailed Report on Party Members Petitioning in the Provincial Capital

More than one hundred party members in this county, including Geng Boyang, believed that Zhang Tingjie and others on the Party Committee were manipulating party affairs and engaging in self-interest and corruption. With the Sixth County Representative Congress about to open, Zhang and others, in order to cling to their positions, specially sent people to Anhui Province and neighboring counties to contact and recruit more than eighty party members to come to Gaoyou to participate in the election. Geng and others repeatedly reported this to the Provincial Party Department according to law. Subsequently, the Provincial Party Department ordered Zhang and others not to transfer Anhui and other county party members to Gaoyou and scheduled the representative meeting to be held on September 15th. Seeing that they were about to be defeated, Zhang and others repeatedly went to the provincial capital to lobby for a postponement in order to find ways to communicate with the various party members. Because the representative meeting was not held on schedule and the provincial supervisor had not arrived in Gaoyou, party members Geng Boyang and others, along with more than seventy party members, went to the provincial capital on the 15th. At 8:00 AM on the 16th, they went to the Provincial Party Department to petition. Because Provincial Executive Committee member Zhou Shaocheng and others were out on official business at that time, they were received by alternate Executive Committee member Chen Kanghe. Geng and others questioned Chen as to why he had not arrived in Gaoyou to supervise the election on schedule. Chen replied that he had not received an appointment order and could not go to Gaoyou. Geng and others refuted him one by one, and Chen was left speechless. He then drafted a resignation from his position as supervisor in Gaoyou. When the party members caught a glimpse of this draft, they all questioned Chen, asking why he was now resigning if he had not been appointed, clearly showing a contradiction. Chen remained silent throughout. The various staff members of the Provincial Party Department then mediated, and the party members dispersed. However, when they arrived in the reception room, they suddenly saw Zhang Tingjie and others also following them to the provincial capital to lobby. The party members stopped and refused to leave. At that time, Provincial Executive Committee member Zhang Gongren happened to enter from outside and brought Zhang Tingjie and Chen Jiaxiang, representing the petitioning party members, to the Standing Committee's office for talks. Chen Jiaxiang first detailed Zhang and others' self-interest and corruption in Gaoyou, and then Zhang stood up to defend himself. Finally, the Provincial Committee slightly reprimanded Zhang, and everyone left the Provincial Party Department. On the morning of the 19th, the Provincial Party Department held an Executive Committee meeting and decided that the County Representative Congress would be held on October 12th and would not be postponed again. The petitioning party members were satisfied and returned to Gaoyou last night (the 20th).

Nantong 83

Judicial Committee Comes to Nantong for Inspection

The Jiangsu Higher Court dispatched a committee member, Zhu Zhongqi, to Nantong to inspect judicial organs. On the 22nd, he went to the County Court, the Fourth Prison, and the Detention Center for inspection. He left Nantong for Shanghai that night.

Department Order to Reorganize Automobile Transport in Northern Jiangsu 84

The Department of Construction, considering that automobile drivers in northern Jiangsu (Nantong, Rugao, Haimen, Taixian, Jingjiang) frequently caused accidents and overturned vehicles, injuring people, specially ordered the county magistrates to consult on reorganization measures and implement them earnestly. The county magistrates are currently meeting in Tongcheng.

Hangzhou 85

Security Bureau Executes Two Kidnappers by Shooting

The Zhejiang Provincial Security Bureau, due to the kidnapping of Cao Along, the young son of Cao Jijing of Shicun Cao Village in Xiaoshan, by Fang Sandwaizi (Fang the shorty) in collusion with Zhu Lixiang, Li Cailang (Li Qianlao), and Hua Along on the night of August 9th of last year, who was hidden in the home of Wang Ziqing in Shanghai, sent detectives to Shanghai to arrest Zhu Lixiang and Li Cailang and rescued the kidnapped person, Cao Ayu, from Wang Ziqing's home, along with Wang Ziqing's wife, Wang Zhushi, and sent personnel to escort them to the Bureau. At that time, the kidnapped person, Cao Ayu, was returned to Cao Jijing. According to the confessions of the two criminals, Zhu and Li, which were undeniable, except that Wang Ziqing and Zhushi were unaware of the situation beforehand, they were transferred to the court for trial. Li Cailang and Zhu Lixiang were sentenced to death according to law. Yesterday (the 23rd) at 10:00 AM, the two bandits were brought out, their identities were verified, and they were escorted to a vacant lot outside Qingbo Gate and executed by shooting.

Special Article: Preface to the Shaanxi Yinluo Project Plan, by Li Xie 86

The Guanzhong Plain is a fertile land, extremely beneficial for agriculture. Its soil is yellow, but it is threatened by drought. The Weibei Plain has already benefited from the Jinghui Canal, and now there are plans to divert the Luo River. I am a child of the Luo River area. Every time I climb high and look deep, I sigh that time passes like this, without being able to make use of it. Considering the failure of the Longshou Canal during the Han Dynasty (please read the History of the Han Dynasty, Records of Canals and Ditches), I did not dare to advocate it empty-handedly. However, Zheng has the achievements of previous sages, making it easier to gain people's trust. Therefore, for ten years, I have focused on diverting the Jing River. Fortunately, with the power of the state and the help of society, success was celebrated. To date, branch canals are not yet widespread, but 500,000 mu have already been irrigated. With the development of water conservancy, agricultural experts and industrialists have come one after another to assist farmers in expanding their careers. How can I not be delighted? Several years ago, people from Dali offered a plan to open a canal. At that time, the focus was on the Jing project, and there was no time to look east. Last year, the Jing Canal was already releasing water, so I resigned from the Department of Construction to devote myself to water conservancy. The Water Conservancy Bureau was established, and I immediately sent two engineers, Fu Jian and Chen Jing, to explore the secluded valleys along the Luo River, as well as the Baishui Nan River. At that time, I was already ill. Fu and Chen returned and reported to me the outline. I then gave instructions on the pillow, drawing lines on the map, and had them remeasure to find the site for diverting water between the large and small valleys, following the river and ravines to tunnel through the Iron Chain Mountains and reach the plains of Dali and Chaoyi. In the past, when the Han Dynasty tunneled the Longshou Canal, they followed the right bank of the Luo River. Because the soil was high, they dug wells section by section to reach Longyang. Its failure was also due to the fact that the soil was too deep and untamed, and the water flowed through it, causing it to collapse. Now, my plan is different from the ancients. Taking the left bank, the original terrain is lower and flatter, and there are many ravines, making it easier to save on earthwork. Fu and Chen remeasured the water level from the valleys and reached the plains at Hancun. They then returned with a sketch, and I was certain that it could be done. I told Chairman Yang, "The Jinghui Canal was completed by your hand. Will you also complete the Luohui Canal?" Chairman Yang was delighted and urged me to move forward with all my might, but I was already very ill again. Knowing that my carbuncle was dangerous, I transferred Sun Shaozong, the deputy chief engineer of the Jinghui Canal, and recommended him to Chairman Yang to serve as the chief engineer and take full responsibility. I then moved into the hospital. Later, I lingered in bed. Chairman Yang, together with Sun and other experts, went to survey and assess. Soon, the Luohui Canal Engineering Bureau was established in Dali. After seven months of surveying and design, the plan was completed. Chairman Yang and Sun frequently visited my bedside to report on the progress and comfort me. My illness improved slightly, and I rested at the Confucius Temple in Xi'an, where I was able to read books. Sun then presented the plan. At that time, the newly appointed Chairman Shao Gong Lizi came to inspect it and praised the meticulous design and precise calculations, saying that he would definitely continue Chairman Yang's aspirations and vigorously promote its implementation. According to the plan, a dam will be built at Lao, diverting water through a canal that is more than 20 kilometers long to reach the plains. There, a diversion gate will be set up, dividing the canal into three. One is the East Main Canal, which runs east to the Yellow River Beach, more than 28 kilometers long. One is the West Main Canal, which runs west into the Luo River, more than 12 kilometers long. One is the Central Main Canal, which runs south to Changjiapo, 6 kilometers long. From there, it will be divided into east and west canals, a total of 32 kilometers long. From these main canals, it will be divided into tributaries to irrigate the fields, potentially 500,000 mu. The estimated cost is only 1,215,000 national currency. My initial plan was to build a bridge across the Luo River and divert water from the West Main Canal to irrigate the southern border of Pucheng. However, whether the water allocation is allowed is subject to the continued observation of the Luo River water measurement station. The land through which the Jing and Wei rivers flow is the same cotton-producing area, with Dali and Chaoyi being particularly prosperous. The quality of the cotton is comparable to American cotton. In the future, the Jinghui Canal will be expanded, and the Luohui Canal will be completed as soon as possible. There will be more than one million mu of good cotton fields, and each mu can harvest one dan of ginned cotton, that is, one million dan of cotton that can be spun into fine yarn can be produced each year. How can its contribution to the national economy be small? Now, before the plan is printed, I will write this preface. Written by Li Xie at the Nanjing Lizhi Society on September 21, 1933.

Mayor Wu Inspected the City's Police Yesterday Morning

The Troops Exercised in the Light Rain with Unwavering Spirit; Wu's Instructions Said That They Should Work Harder in the Future

The Shanghai Municipal Police Department originally scheduled to inspect the city's police force at the Public Sports Ground on the 20th of this month. However, due to the arrangement not being completed as scheduled, it was rescheduled to 9:00 AM yesterday morning at the same location, with Mayor Wu and Director Wen conducting the inspection. However, it was drizzling and the ground was extremely muddy. However, the spirit of the various teams exercising did not diminish in the slightest. The details are recorded separately below:

Attendees 93

In addition to Mayor Wu, Director Wen, Chief Inspector Li Guangzeng, Deputy Chief Inspector Dong Pingyu, Detective Squad Leader Lu Ying, Secretary Li Mo, First Section Chief Lin Wenquan, Second Section Chief Hong Qi, District Chief Guan Gong of the First District, District Chief Li Jing of the Second District, District Chief Zhang Hongqin of the Third District, District Chief Lai Gang of the Fourth District, District Chief Jin Gong of the Fifth District, District Chief Tan Baoshou of the Sixth District, District Chief Gong Xiukui of the Seventh District, and the various branch chiefs, there were also Secretary Zhang Tingrong of the Municipal Government, Regiment Commander Chen Zhuomin of the First Regiment of the Security Bureau, Deputy Regiment Commander Wen Huazhou, and more than fifty others.

Participating Teams 94

The teams participating in the inspection included the First and Second Pistol Squads, 300 men, and a Machine Gun Squad, 150 men, lined up on the left side of the reviewing stand. The Patrol Squad, 50 men, lined up on the right side of the reviewing stand. There were also about 1,000 police officers from the various districts and precincts of the Police Brigade, lined up opposite the reviewing stand. The district chiefs and precinct chiefs of each district formed a two-person row in front of the reviewing stand. Mayor Wu, Director Wen, and guests inspected the teams on the stand.

Stand Arrangement 95

The reviewing stand was in the center of the east side of the venue, a reed mat shed. A sound system was temporarily installed on the stand, with a portrait of Sun Yat-sen in the center. Various slogans were posted on both sides, such as "Sincerely Love the People," "Strictly Abide by Police Discipline," "Protect Public Security," "Enforce National Laws," "Develop a Revolutionary Spirit," "Eliminate Bureaucratic Habits," "Obey the Orders of Superiors," etc.

Conduct of the Inspection 96

At 9:00 AM, the Shanghai Municipal Police Department's military band played music, and the teams entered the venue in an orderly fashion, lining up according to their assigned positions. The parade began, with the orders issued by General Commander Hong Liang and Deputy Commander Li Beiwu. The first was a pass in review (the police officers from the various districts and precincts did not participate), followed by company-level training, platoon combat training, machine gun company-level training, broadsword team martial arts, etc. After the exercises were completed, Mayor Wu and Director Wen delivered speeches. After the speeches, the grand exercise was held and the event ended.

Mayor's Address 97

Mayor Wu gave an address, saying: Director Wen, all police officers, soldiers, and gentlemen, our country is so vast and our people so numerous. What methods should we use to maintain the survival of the nation and its people, and to protect the order of peaceful life for the people? There are roughly two forces: one is military force and the other is law. The force of arms is the military, and the force of peace is the law. The military is used to resist foreign aggression. When foreign forces invade and coerce our nation, we use the power of the military to resist. Therefore, the duty of soldiers is to resist foreign aggression. However, in times of peace, we must use the power of the law to maintain the order of the country and society. Laws are dead letters; they cannot be executed on their own; they rely entirely on human effort. But who will execute the law? That is the responsibility of us police. Whether the police can shoulder this responsibility depends on their knowledge and ability. The world is advancing day by day, and society and human affairs are becoming increasingly complex. Therefore, the responsibility of the police is also becoming increasingly heavy. The knowledge and ability of the police must increase day by day with the world and society in order to cope with the advancing world and the complex society. Our country is still in the process of construction. In this process, every country is bound to experience great turmoil. This can be proven by history, both in China and abroad. This kind of turmoil is an inevitable stage for every country to go through from chaos to order, from weakness to strength. If we want to reduce this turmoil, we need the police even more. The police are an organization distributed throughout society and are in constant contact with the people. If the police are knowledgeable and capable, their greatest effectiveness is to eliminate, as much as possible, all dangers lurking in the deepest layers of society that are harmful to the society, the country, and the people, and to maintain the peace and order of society with the law and protect the safety of the region. Conversely, if the police organization is not strict, its knowledge is unsound, and its capabilities are too weak, it will certainly not be able to achieve this greatest effectiveness. We see that among the police across the country today, there are those who are unable to meet the expectations of the government and the people, all because their organization is not strict and their knowledge and abilities are shallow. Their greatest effectiveness is only to stop illegal and criminal behavior in society. Some are even unable to stop criminal activity after it has occurred. The greatest effectiveness of the police lies in eliminating all dangers before they occur. As a last resort, when danger erupts, they must be able to immediately stop it and reduce it, preventing it from expanding. If the effectiveness of the police is only to stop it after the fact, then such police are equivalent to being non-existent and are not the kind of police needed by the country, society, and the people. Take the January 28th Shanghai Incident last year, for example. At that time, there were many reactionaries and traitors who wanted to take advantage of the opportunity of the January 28th war and foreign forces to seize power, subvert the government, and endanger society and the country. Fortunately, the Shanghai police at that time were able to uncover and eliminate the organizations and institutions of traitors and reactionaries in advance, preventing them from harming the region and the country. This finally achieved a bit of the maximum effect of the police. The expenses and salaries of our police all come from the people's taxes. The people have the obligation to pay taxes, and at the same time, they have the right to demand that the government fully protect their lives and property. Since the expenses and salaries of our police come from the people, we must constantly reflect and examine the work we each do every day to see if it meets the expectations of the people. If we find that the work we do every day still does not meet the expectations of the people and there are shortcomings, we must always try our best to make up for our shortcomings and satisfy the people. This is the duty of you policemen. The government and the people expect so much and so urgently from our police, so we policemen must never fail them or fail in our duties, because the police are different from other officials. They are the officials closest to the people, distributed throughout society, and in daily contact with the people. Therefore, if they can fulfill their responsibilities, everyone will see it. If they fail in their duties, everyone will also see it. Doing good deeds will be praised by the people, and doing bad deeds will be criticized by the people. I have been a county magistrate and worked in the police force for several years. I believe that the work of all officials that can best win the attention and praise of society is that of the police and the county magistrate, because the police and the county magistrate are also the officials closest to the people. They have to deal directly with everything in society, and they must have sufficient knowledge and ability to deal with everything. Therefore, they can also improve their knowledge and ability the most while serving. As long as we policemen and county magistrates can be loyal to our duties, we will definitely increase a lot of knowledge and ability, and we will definitely be able to shoulder greater responsibilities in the future. Now you are all police officers or soldiers. This is not only a very honorable position, but also a good opportunity for you to demonstrate your knowledge and ability, and also to increase your knowledge and ability. Why do I say that being a police officer or soldier is very honorable? Because the duty of our police is to directly serve the people and society and seek the welfare of others. This is what I feel is very honorable and rare. Therefore, you must respect your own position, improve your character, and fully demonstrate your knowledge and ability, so that the people of society feel that they can sleep soundly when there are police. If you cannot do good things, you must not do bad things. This is the most important thing. Of course, it is very hopeful that you will do good things that benefit the country, society, and the people, not only fulfilling your duties but also allowing the people to enjoy welfare. The reason why we inspect the police every year is to inspect the knowledge and ability of the police, whether they can carry out their important tasks, and to let society know whether the effectiveness of the police is improving year by year. The past year or two has been the most dangerous and chaotic period in the history of Shanghai, and the Shanghai police have been relatively competent and generally good. However, we cannot be complacent about this, nor can we say that we can satisfy the expectations of society and the people. Therefore, we should work harder in the future to maintain the previous honor of the Shanghai police.

[Photo caption: Mayor Wu inspects the city police (photographed by Qichang)]

Director Wen's Address 98

After Mayor Wu's address, Director Wen gave an address, saying roughly: Under Mayor Wu's constant guidance, the city's police administration has become increasingly substantial and police discipline has become increasingly thorough. Today, we are once again honored by Mayor Wu's personal inspection and address. All police officers and soldiers in the city should deeply engrave it in their minds and use it as a guide for our service at all times. Among Mayor Wu's addresses, what we must not forget is that the mission of the police is to maintain local security and protect the lives and property of citizens by law and with arms. Although the police and the military both belong to the armed forces, the military is for resisting foreign aggression, while the police are for maintaining local security according to the law. All our police officers and soldiers are supported by the people, so we should do our best to protect the safety of the people, etc.

Longhai Railway and China Merchants Bureau

Signing a Contract for Sea-Land Intermodal Transport 99

Shipments from the Northwest to Shanghai Will Become More Convenient / Intermodal Location is Laoyao Near Haizhou

The Longhai Railway is making concrete progress in developing transport in the Northwest, opening up Lianyungang, adding the new Xugou port, and implementing sea-land intermodal transport to develop Northwest traffic. The new port is currently under construction and will be fully completed next year. This year, the shipping industry on all routes has been sluggish, but the Haizhou route has been able to maintain itself without loss due to the increased export of goods from the Northwest. Ships sailing to Haizhou from Shanghai can all make a profit. The Longhai Railway Bureau recently sent personnel to Shanghai at the invitation of the China Merchants Bureau to sign a sea-land intermodal transport contract. The contract was signed yesterday afternoon. In the future, the sea transport of goods entering and leaving the Northwest, which are transferred by the Railway Bureau, will be handled exclusively by China Merchants. The details are as follows:

Current Merchant Ships 100

On the Shanghai-Haizhou route, the regular scheduled ships operating from Shanghai were originally the Yongping, Yongan, and Yongji of the Dazhen Shipping Company, and the Zhengzhou, Xuzhou, and Haizhou of the Nanshi Hezhong Shipping Company. The China Merchants Bureau originally sent the Tonghua ship to operate. These seven regular ships all go to Dapu Port to load goods. There are also 11 or 12 other irregular temporary cargo ships and salt-carrying ships each month. However, these "wild chicken" ships have no fixed routes or schedules and are not permanently within the Shanghai sea route. Only the seven ships of the three companies operate regularly and never change.

Establishing Intermodal Transport 101

The China Merchants Bureau, with its state-owned nature, has been promoting the shipping industry. This year, the Puan ship has been operating to Qingdao and has begun to sign an intermodal transport contract with the Jiaoji Railway. In recent months, the results have been very good and convenient for passengers. Now, it has further negotiated with the Longhai Railway to sign a sea-land intermodal transport contract. All goods transported from Shanghai to the Northwest and goods from the Northwest are transferred by the Longhai Railway. The sea transport of the Shanghai-Haizhou section is handled exclusively by the China Merchants Bureau. The two sides have been discussing this for a long time. Now, in order to implement it as soon as possible, the two parties have formally signed the revised draft intermodal transport contract.

One Year Trial 102

The Longhai Railway Bureau has decided to implement sea-land intermodal transport from October 1. All procedures have been completed. After the draft agreement was revised, it immediately commissioned Mr. Zhou, the person in charge of transport operations, to come to Shanghai. At 10:00 a.m. yesterday, he met with Liu Hongsheng at the China Merchants Bureau Headquarters and formally signed the sea-land intermodal transport contract. Each party holds one copy. Starting next month, the contract will be performed in accordance with the agreement. In the future, all goods transported by China Merchants Bureau ships to the Northwest will be transported by the Longhai Railway Bureau, and goods from the Northwest will be transferred to Shanghai by China Merchants Bureau ships. The trial period will last until the end of September next year. If both parties agree to renew the intermodal transport, a new agreement will be signed again.

Intermodal Location 103

Haizhou Dapu was originally a port for merchant ships, but in recent years, it has become too silted up, and heavily loaded ships with deeper drafts often run aground. Therefore, the new Xugou port is being built. However, before the new port is completed, the Longhai Railway Bureau has established a temporary pier at Laoyao Seaport, 40 kilometers from Dapu, for the convenience of loading and unloading goods for intermodal transport. It has also built temporary warehouses and extended the Longhai Railway branch line to Laoyao, making it a temporary port for sea-land intermodal transport. Starting next month, China Merchants Bureau ships to Haizhou will go directly to Laoyao, which will avoid the obstruction of Dapu Seaport. In the future, goods from the Northwest can also be unloaded at Laoyao, which can moor large seagoing vessels and is not restricted by the port.

China Merchants Increases Ships 104

China Merchants originally sent one ship to the Haizhou route, either Tonghua or Jiahe, which was designated at any time from the two ships. Now that the intermodal transport contract has been signed, the import and export of goods from the Northwest will inevitably be more than it is now. The Bureau's business on the Haizhou route will also expand accordingly. The original dispatch of one ship is no longer sufficient. The Bureau is now considering increasing the number of seagoing vessels, and will temporarily transfer them after inspecting the situation on each route. It is estimated that at least one or two more ships will be needed to meet the demand. Before the new seagoing vessels being built arrive in Shanghai, they will generally be transferred from the North and South Ocean routes.

Shipping Companies Object 105

The China Merchants Bureau's signing of a sea-land intermodal transport contract with the Longhai Railway has been opposed by the Sanbei Company in this city. There are many Chinese merchant ships operating on the Haizhou route in Shanghai, and their cargo depends entirely on goods from the Northwest. Now that the Bureau monopolizes the advantages of intermodal transport, other merchant ships on the same route will have no goods to transport in the future. The Dazhen Hezhong and other companies have also expressed their opposition to this matter. However, the person in charge of the China Merchants Bureau said that the Bureau is a state-owned institution and seems to be different from commercially operated shipping companies. There are many precedents for intermodal transport in various countries, such as the South Manchuria Railway and Dalian Steamship Company, and the Japanese Post and the Ministry of Railways. There seems to be no reason for the opposition of the shipping companies.

The Times Comments

Telephone Company's Price Increase Cannot be Increased Before the End of the Three Years / Must Present Solid Evidence 109

The Shanghai Times commented yesterday on the Shanghai Telephone Company's application to the authorities of the two concessions for a price increase, saying roughly, "The public seems to be unaware that when the authorities of the two concessions signed a contract with the Telephone Company in 1930, granting it exclusive operating rights, it was stipulated that the original prices would continue to be charged until the complete conversion to automatic telephones. Within three years after the complete conversion (i.e., until March 1935), prices would be charged according to the construction prices specified in the Anthon report. After the three-year period, the telephone rates would be revised according to the operating conditions, so that the company's invested capital could obtain a 10% interest rate. The Municipal Council must be well aware of this provision. We do not understand why the Municipal Council did not inform the company of the contract terms when it applied for a price increase, urging it to wait a little longer and not rush. Now that this matter has been submitted to the Public Utilities Committee for consideration, this provision must be pointed out more solemnly. The amount of the increase and the date of implementation requested by the company have not yet been announced, but one point must be raised on behalf of the public: the Municipal Council, as the protector of the public, should not lightly grant the increase unless the company can present full accounts proving that it will face permanent financial difficulties within the remaining 30 years of the exclusive operating period if the price is not increased immediately. We still remember that when the company increased prices last year in accordance with the contract, it aroused opposition and indignation from the citizens. Moreover, it is worth noting that when the Chinese side recently requested the cancellation of the five-cent Chinese-foreign call fee, the company believed that since there was a contract, it must be observed and not changed unilaterally. Otherwise, what would be the benefit of signing contracts in the future? This principle of observing contracts should also be applicable to the provisions on telephone rates. The main purpose of the Anthon investigation report was to protect the public interest and stipulate a five-year trial period to observe the company's financial situation. Now that the trial period is only 18 months away, will the prices stipulated in the contract cause such a large loss that it cannot wait a moment and must be remedied immediately? Now, after 1935, the company still has 35 years of exclusive operating rights to collect the due remuneration. As for the telephone rates for users, they have already been increased once. If the stipulated three-year period has not yet expired, and it wants to increase them a second time, is that not an unfair way? Although we are not saying that the company's reasons should not be given a fair hearing at present, we believe that there must be solid evidence to prove that the company will face irreparable financial difficulties if the contract is not allowed to be changed before it can be allowed to increase prices."

Fessenden Visited Yu Hongjun Yesterday

Factory Inspection Involves Chinese Sovereignty / The Municipal Council Warns Factories Must Be Cautious / Therefore, the Meeting Yesterday Resulted in No Progress 110

Fessenden, Director-General of the Public Concession Municipal Council, visited Secretary-General Yu Hongjun of the Municipal Government at 11:00 a.m. yesterday to continue discussions on the issue of factory inspections in the concession. There were disputes over the issue of sovereignty over the jurisdiction of the inspection team. Yu also advised the Municipal Council not to arbitrarily warn Chinese factories in the concession. The two discussed for an hour. The content is as follows:

Jurisdiction of the Inspection Team 111

Yesterday, Fessenden visited Yu and first said that the Municipal Council Board of Directors could express its approval of the measures proposed by the two for the negotiation results, but the issue of jurisdiction after the inspection team was organized should be discussed. The Municipal Council intends to follow the measures for stamp taxes on tobacco and alcohol in the concession, with the Municipal Council managing on behalf. After hearing this, Yu replied reasonably, saying, "The right to inspect factories in the concession belongs to the Chinese government. However, the Chinese government, for the sake of the welfare of workers, ordered me to negotiate with the Municipal Council for handling, not hesitating to compromise in every way. Each side sent personnel to form an inspection team. Our side has already made many concessions. If there are opinions and disputes among the inspectors, the two secretaries-general can impartially adjudicate them. According to the Municipal Council's claim, it concerns our sovereignty and is not possible to negotiate," etc. It is heard that our side upholds the established principle and will never lose sovereignty. Fessenden still has to take orders from the Board of Directors. The measures agreed upon by the two sides previously have no possibility of proceeding.

Caution in Warning Factories 112

Yu also expressed his views to Fessenden regarding the Municipal Council's recent arbitrary warnings to Chinese factories in the concession, saying, "The Municipal Government, for the sake of the welfare of workers and to eliminate public danger, sympathizes with the Municipal Council's warnings to factories. However, the right to manage factories in the concession belongs to our side. The meaning of Article 34 of the Annex to the Yangjingbang Regulations is very narrow, limited only to the Municipal Council's ability to ban dangerous buildings. The Municipal Council should not use this as a basis to arbitrarily warn Chinese factories in the concession. It is hoped that this will be handled cautiously in the future." Fessenden expressed his agreement to consider this point and handle it carefully in the future, and then excused himself and left.

In addition, the Shanghai-Ningbo telegraph line, which was damaged by the wind, was also repaired the day before yesterday.
