Duke Wang Requests the Municipal Government to Strictly Arrest Impersonators of the Righteous Army 115

The Shanghai Liaison Office of the Third Route Commander of the Northeast Anti-Japanese Volunteer Army received an order from Commander Wang from Dongbeigou, Rehe West, yesterday, and a letter to Mayor Wu. The letter is as follows: "Sir, since the September 18th Incident, the troops of our Route have been engaged in anti-Japanese work, fighting bloody battles for many years and sacrificing greatly. They are still stationed in the Rehe West area, participating in the recovery of lost territory. Because news from the rear is often blocked, liaison offices have been established in Beiping, Guangzhou, Nanjing, and Shanghai to facilitate matters. This has been reported to the General Commander of our Army, Zhu Zhaozhun, for approval. However, according to a report from the Shanghai Liaison Office, there are now lawless elements, falsely claiming the name of our Route, swaggering and deceiving people everywhere, and even impersonating the echelon commander of our Route. This is shocking. Our Route only has the First and Second Columns, and there is no echelon system. Moreover, all levels of military officers of our Route are working with the General Commander of our Army at the front. How can anyone dare to impersonate? Obviously, there are other motives, seeking donations for profit. Such behavior is a serious violation of the law, and it damages the reputation of our Route and insults the personality of the Righteous Army. It is even more outrageous. In addition to ordering the Shanghai Liaison Office to immediately publish a notice in the newspaper, not to be deceived, we also ordered them to submit a letter to you, requesting your Municipal Government to investigate and arrest these lawless elements strictly, in order to deter lawlessness and maintain the reputation of the army. This is a public convenience. Correspondingly, we send this letter, requesting your attention and implementation. Respectfully, [addressed to] Mayor Wu of the Shanghai Municipal Government, Wang Gongwei, Commander of the Third Route of the Northeast Anti-Japanese Volunteer Army, September 18th."

Disasters Reported Everywhere / Baoshan 116

Changxingsha and other areas belonging to Baoshan County, isolated at sea, were suddenly hit by a typhoon on the 2nd of this month, suffering extremely heavy damage. The Baoshan County Government convened a joint meeting of various agencies, and the Property Management Office first raised 1,000 yuan to purchase supplies and dispatched personnel to distribute emergency relief. At the same time, the Provincial Government was telegraphed to allocate funds for relief. Unexpectedly, less than half a month later, on the night of September 18, the typhoon struck again. The wind rode the tide, and the tide rode the wind, with the water level two or three feet higher than on September 2. People and animals drifted away, forming an unprecedented disaster. The sand people had no place to live and lacked clothing and food, and they flocked across the sea to the city to request relief. The County Government, supervised by the First District Office, took them in and provided them with supplies. However, the various agencies of the County, since the January 28th war, have been in dire financial straits. The previous request for relief from the Province has not been addressed. This time, the disaster is even worse, and relief cannot be delayed. The County Government convened another meeting and decided that, in addition to telegraphing the Provincial Government again for relief, Gu's Mansion would also prepare a letter and send personnel to discuss with various charitable organizations for maximum assistance. Yan Guangen, Zhou Zhizhen, Jiang Hongbin, Zhu Yiyi, and other gentlemen were appointed as representatives to contact the Shanghai Chinese and Foreign Relief Society, the Shanghai Jisheng Society, Renjitang, the Chinese Red Cross Society, the Shanghai Red Swastika Society, and other organizations to request assistance. It is heard that the various charitable organizations are working to provide relief.

Nanhui 117

The Chinese Jisheng Society recently received a telegram from Jia Rida, the County Magistrate and Disaster Relief Committee of Nanhui County, stating, "Our County suffered a typhoon disaster on the 1st and 2nd of this month, and we telegraphed for allocation of funds to relieve the disaster victims on the *th of this month. We are currently rushing to repair the sea dikes, and the pear wind suddenly brought rain, intensifying at night, uprooting trees and collapsing houses, layer upon layer. The wind is more violent than the last time. The urban area is like this, and the disaster situation along the coast is unimaginable. By Haoshang morning, the wind had subsided slightly, but the rain had not stopped. We urgently appeal, begging you to quickly raise funds for relief, to have pity on the disaster victims," etc. According to reports, the Society is providing relief to the disaster-stricken areas of Baoshan Wusong, the sandbanks of the Yangtze River, and the islands of Chuansha. The second typhoon and heavy rain have arrived, and the disaster situation has doubled. The lives, livestock, property, and other losses of the people are incalculable. The disaster areas of Qidong, Nanhui, Haimen, and other places are even more tragic. How can we compare them to the Henan flood and the East Yellow River water disaster? The Society is currently discussing with the Ten Charity Groups to solicit donations and record names, in the hope of saving more disaster victims and establishing good relationships. It is hoped that saving lives is not just benefiting one province or one county, but creating endless blessings.

Zhenhai 118

The Zhenhai Embankment Works Bureau sent a telegram to the Ningbo Fellow-Townsmen Association in Shanghai, addressed to all gentlemen of the Ningbo community in Shanghai: Our county experienced fierce winds and torrential rains on the night of the 18th of this month, with a sudden surge in the tide, turning both the city and the countryside into a watery expanse. The ferocity of the disaster surpasses even the floods and typhoons of the Republic of China Year 20, constituting a massive calamity unseen in a century. Among the most pressing concerns requiring urgent repair is the Wan Gong Embankment, the protective barrier for the six counties along the rear sea. Investigations reveal that the embankment, previously repaired after sections were damaged through fundraising, has suffered further damage. The tide exceeded the embankment by three to four feet. Not only have the unrepaired sections deteriorated, but the newly repaired sections have also been battered and shattered by the wind and tides. After thorough inspection by Hou Pei and others, it is estimated that approximately 1,600 zhang of the stone embankment, stretching from Jinzi Mountain to Yu Fan Road, has sustained damage, with about 200 zhang severely affected, rendering the entire embankment in a precarious state. We plan to prioritize urgent repairs to prevent unforeseen circumstances. The estimated cost of the project is around thirty to forty thousand yuan. In addition to reporting the disaster to the county government, we are sending this telegram in advance. Further details will be provided in a subsequent letter. Respectfully, Li Houpei, Director of the Zhenhai County Embankment Works Bureau, Jiang Yichang, Deputy Director, and others.

Yin County 119

The Seventh District of Yin County sent a telegram to the Ningbo Fellow-Townsmen Association in Shanghai, addressed to all gentlemen of the Ningdu Shanghai Fellow-Townsmen Association: Fierce winds and torrential rains struck here on the afternoon of the 17th of this month, ceasing only on the morning of the 19th. The mountains and rivers along the Yin River overflowed, turning the area into a watery expanse. Fields and villages were submerged, and livestock were swept away. The autumn harvest is now hopeless. Roads, embankments, and weirs have been largely destroyed. All utility poles have been snapped, cutting off transportation. Countless houses and appliances have been collapsed by the flood. Overall, the severity of this disaster and the magnitude of the losses are comparable to those of the Republic of China Year 10. Although the floodwaters have receded, the disaster has already occurred. A chorus of cries for help awaits assistance. Apart from the accurate figures for losses, which will be gathered and reported later, we are sending this telegram to request your esteemed association to consider our shared native-place ties and devise appropriate relief measures. The fellow townsmen would be immensely grateful. This urgent telegram conveys our pressing need for assistance. Mao Dushi, District Head of the Seventh District of Yin County.

Tianjin 120

The China Foreign Famine Relief Committee reported that it received a representative from the South Hebei Huanghe (Yellow River) Relief Committee of Changyuan County, Hebei Province, Han Zhensheng, who provided a face-to-face account of the disaster in Changyuan County, Hebei Province. A record of this situation is provided below: (1) The volume of the Yellow River this year is unprecedented in history. On August 11th, both banks of the river in Changyuan County breached simultaneously for more than forty miles. On the west bank, from the Third to the Fifth District, there were thirty-two breaches along approximately thirty miles. There were also multiple breaches on the east bank. (2) The water's force was fierce. When the levees first breached, the water level was between one to two zhang high in some places and several feet high in others. In an instant, the entire county was submerged, turning over 800 villages into a watery expanse. Fortunately, most people were able to escape. (3) The flooded area covers over 800 villages and over 14,000 qing of farmland. (4) The affected population is over 300,000, with approximately four to five percent drowned. (5) Floating grains, along with stored grains in warehouses, were completely swept away, with losses estimated at over 15 million yuan. (6) Drowned livestock: The total number of livestock in the county is estimated at over 70,000. Approximately 70% of these animals have been drowned, drifted away, or starved to death, with losses estimated at 800,000 head. (7) Clothing, farming tools, etc., that were washed away are valued at several million yuan. (8) Collapsed houses: There are approximately 600,000 houses in the entire county, with approximately 500,000 of them collapsed by the water. The loss is valued at approximately 1 million yuan. (9) Altered land: The land near the river was known for its fertility, with each mu worth up to 100 yuan. However, the Yellow River's waters have inundated and silted these lands, transforming them into sand-blown fields, accounting for about one-third of the county's land. This is a permanent change, and the extent of the loss cannot be estimated. (10) The livelihoods of the disaster victims: Most are currently taking refuge on high ground or in collapsed and dilapidated houses, often exposed to the elements. They endure scorching sun and chilling winds while excavating spoiled grain and gathering bridge railings to fill their stomachs. Most tragically, heavy rains have followed the flood. Some use mats as shelters or build grass huts, while others are simply exposed to the rain. Some go without fire for one or two days, their cries of hunger and cold bringing tears to the eyes and piercing the heart. The wretchedness and sorrow of their plight are unbearable to describe fully. In summary, the magnitude of the losses from the Changyuan County flood is immense. Apart from the inestimable cost of fertile land transformed into sand-blown fields, the losses are estimated at approximately 25 million yuan. The number of people killed or injured is estimated to be in the tens of thousands, while 300,000 disaster victims are without shelter, clothing, or food. Their movements are restricted by the danger of silted beaches and deep waters. Even after the Yellow River recedes, the opportunity to sow wheat will be limited by a lack of seeds. Exposed to the scorching sun and wind and rain, eating rotten grain and drinking foul water, a major epidemic is inevitable. It is feared that the 300,000 people will not only die from hunger and cold but also from the epidemic. These wailing souls urgently need help.

Shanghai Red Cross Relief Team Headed North Yesterday 121

In light of the severe Yellow River flood disaster, the Shanghai Red Cross Society, through the efforts of various philanthropists such as Zhang Qianmiao, He Qianren, Qi Minlin, and Huang Jiwu, has collected 20,000 yuan in relief funds. Qi Minlin and Zhao Lin were publicly elected to lead a team, including member He Hongyu and laborers, to Jinan to make arrangements. Mr. Qi left for the north by the express train last night. The presidents of the society and various philanthropists saw them off at the station. Before departing, Messrs. Qi and Zhao declared to those seeing them off that their trip would adhere to the principle of charitable relief, saving the dying without helping the poor. They would handle urgent relief efforts, not accept local supplies or official receptions, and all operations would be coordinated with the Jinan Red Cross Society.

The General Chamber of Commerce Strongly Advocates Taxing Foreign Rice and Rejects a Letter from Cai Xuetian of Shantou 123

The National Federation of Chambers of Commerce rejected a letter from Cai Xuetian of the Shantou Overseas Chinese Daily opposing the Federation's proposal to tax foreign rice. The Federation has sent another letter in response. The original letters are recorded below:

Cai's Letter 124

To all Executive Directors of the National Federation of Chambers of Commerce: I have received your detailed response regarding the matter of levying import duties on foreign rice. Your earnest and sincere intentions are deeply appreciated. Taxing foreign rice affects the people's food supply, and even village elders and children are directly and personally affected. This is an extraordinary measure, and I find myself unable to fully agree with many points in your letter. Thinking of the disaster victims, my heart trembles and my conscience is uneasy. I cannot blindly follow your proposal. I will list my views and hope to learn from your guidance: (1) For over a decade, our country's food imports have been increasing year by year. The statistics from the customs office clearly show that your argument that our country has insufficient food supplies, claiming it may only be in lean years, is not supported by the facts and cannot be used as a basis for proposing this measure. (2) The Chinese people have all experienced the hardship of food shortages. Their lives are below the poverty line, and over 90% are living between life and death. To provide relief, it should not be limited to rice-producing areas (as mentioned in your letter). Taxing foreign rice will burden the rice-consuming population. Even if it increases the price of domestic rice, those who benefit from the higher prices will still be the same suffering people. Every action taken only increases the government's tax revenue and adds to the people's economic hardship. Where is the benefit? (3) The main reason for importing foreign rice is the insufficient domestic food supply. This can be clearly seen in the statistics. Even with heavy taxes, people cannot survive on air. The supply and demand situation remains unchanged. To increase the government's revenue by taxing foreign rice is insufficient to prevent the dumping of foreign rice. (4) The use of tariff barriers is a weapon for protecting production, and there are many examples. However, has China's hard-won tariff autonomy benefited domestic products at all besides providing revenue for the central government? There are numerous ways to collect taxes besides tariffs. Do you think my concern that this bad precedent will lead to taxes on domestic grains is excessive? Please consider the facts and the past events after gaining tariff autonomy, and you will surely stop. (5) The Chinese people have suffered greatly from unified taxes. The consequences are unbearable. During the Hong Yang Rebellion, officials, troubled by military expenses, created the Likin system. This mistake has caused the entire Chinese population to suffer under harsh taxes for over a century. They have endured countless cries, endless humiliation, and countless difficulties. Thanks to foreign intervention, it was finally abolished, but some measures that harm the people remain to compensate for the tax. The beginning may be small, but the cruelty is unparalleled and the long-term impact is worse than massacre. These are lessons that you should learn from. Thinking of the endless harm, I am concerned. (6) Your letter also states that the foreign rice tax will only slightly affect the people of one or two provinces, while benefiting the entire country. So you admit that one or two provinces will be affected. How many people in the country rely on rice for a living? How many people have enough rice to feed themselves, and how many need to buy rice? How different are the gains and losses? What are the trade-offs? You are all respected figures. If you are not fully aware of the situation, how can you make decisions? The way of governing is to be fair. Even if it is only one or two provinces (referring to Fujian and Guangdong), these provinces have over 50 million people, and the impact is huge. Shouldn't there be ways to compensate before taking such drastic measures? (7) The world's economy is heading towards bankruptcy, and our poor country is suffering even more. Prices have been falling in recent years, and although not uniformly, everything is trending downwards. People are already struggling to make ends meet and are facing starvation. Now, you are raising the price of rice, a necessity for survival. A small number of people in rice-producing areas may benefit, but it will be too much for the entire population. (8) There have been reports of taxes on domestic rice. The heavy taxes and fees on farmland are too numerous to name, even for officials. In recent years, government systems have been changing, and local organizations have been expanding, increasing expenses. These expenses are covered by taxes on people and land, which are indirectly levied on agricultural products. Agricultural production has not been addressed, and cultivation methods remain outdated. The cost is high, and the output is low, which is why it cannot compete with foreign rice. Your plan to provide relief is not addressing the root cause. It is merely a temporary solution and not a way to benefit the country and the people. The above eight points are either established facts or verifiable reasons that cannot be concealed or denied. If the government is sincere in helping rice-producing farmers, it should focus on reducing the burden on farmers, lowering agricultural production costs, developing production areas, and increasing production with national support. By using incentives for production and subsidies for sales, the goal of food self-sufficiency can be achieved. If the entire country works together, foreign rice will disappear without taxes. Your association is a group of businessmen, and you are all well-known figures. If you can find a fair and just way to provide relief, the entire country will respond, and future generations will benefit. I hope you will consider this. Sincerely, Cai Xuetian.

The Chamber of Commerce's Reply 125

In response to your previous letter discussing the tax on foreign rice, we have received another letter discussing eight points, insisting that our country has insufficient domestic rice and must rely on foreign rice. You worry that Fujian and Guangdong will become disaster areas after the foreign rice tax and that this bad precedent will lead to taxes on domestic grains. We admire your kindness and foresight. However, our association is considering the entire country and the majority of the people. Therefore, we propose a heavy tariff on foreign rice to treat the symptoms and reduce the cost of domestic rice to treat the root cause. Since we submitted the proposal to the central government, the response from various provincial governments and the support from public opinion, except for foreign rice merchants, has been almost unanimous, indicating that our association's proposal is not wrong. We will reply to your points as follows: (1) We cannot conclude that our country has insufficient food based solely on customs statistics on grain imports. Although there are no precise statistics on the total grain production in our country, we can estimate it. Most provinces north of the Yangtze River eat wheat. After a bumper harvest last year, many people switched from wheat to rice due to the sharp drop in rice prices, resulting in a larger purchase of wheat than rice. This has already been seen in the reports of the Ministry of Industry and the Ministry of Railways. Guizhou, Yunnan, Guizhou, and Sichuan may have deficits or surpluses that can be supplemented. The remaining provinces, including Hunan, Hubei, Jiangxi, Henan, Anhui, and Jiangsu, are all rice-surplus areas. The provinces with a rice deficit are Zhejiang, Fujian, and Guangdong. Zhejiang has a small deficit. According to the declaration of rice merchants in Guangdong last year, about 10 million dan of foreign rice are imported each year. Although there are no statistics for Fujian, it should not exceed the amount of Guangdong. The surplus of six provinces can cover the deficit of three provinces. Even if the deficit is as you said, it should not be much. Moreover, grain prices have been falling in recent years, and farmers have switched to other crops because the harvest cannot cover the cost of labor and fertilizer. If grain prices rise, they will return to the original state, and the production will increase year by year. Furthermore, if our country has a grain shortage, grain prices should have risen first. However, the price of imported grain has fallen, which clearly shows that other countries are dumping surplus grain in our country. Therefore, we cannot conclude that the import of grain through customs meets the needs of our country. (2) Our country is an agricultural country, and farmers should be more numerous than any other profession. If, as you said, (90% are living between life and death,) our association believes that farmers should account for more than 90% of this 90%. To weigh the importance, we should sacrifice 10% to save 90%. Moreover, this 10% may not be sincerely sacrificing themselves. (3) This is due to the subjective error in the first point. Based solely on the statistics of foreign rice imports, you conclude that there is insufficient domestic grain and that people will eat air after the foreign rice tax. This is an overestimation. Did people start eating air after taxes were levied on cloth? (4) Our country has fought for a long time to regain tariff autonomy. The government has just gotten rid of the shackles and has not had time to implement measures. However, the determination of which tax rates should be high and which should be low is to promote domestic production through tariffs. This is very different from being slaughtered before regaining autonomy. Recently, the Ministry of Industry is discussing protective tariffs. This is a good understanding of the government. The fact is that your statement that (besides providing revenue for the central government, has there been any benefit to domestic products?) is far from the truth. The so-called bad precedent that will lead to taxes on domestic grains is an obvious overestimation. Our country is an agricultural country, and agriculture is the foundation of the country. The decline of rural areas means the foundation of the country is shaking. The central government has also paid attention to this. For example, it has explicitly exempted transit taxes and rice inspection fees, and the Ministry of Transportation has reduced freight rates. The Ministry of Industry has sent personnel to investigate and find ways to provide relief. These facts can prove that the central government's actions are the opposite of what you said. (5) The harm of Likin is undeniable. However, it was only used for military expenses at the time. By the Republic of China, it had been listed as national expenditure. If it were abolished, the national expenditure would be insufficient, and we would have to collect business taxes and unified taxes as a transitional compensation. However, whether the unified tax rate is harmful to the people or not will be proven by the facts. Taxing foreign rice has the meaning of providing relief to rural areas and should not be confused with it. (6) The number of people who eat rice cannot be statistically determined, but farmers are more numerous than other people. No one would deny this. The oversupply of domestic grain has been mentioned above, so the number of sellers should be greater than the number of buyers. The so-called impact on one or two provinces is only temporary and they will only eat slightly more expensive rice. This is the same as other foreign goods and will not lead to disaster areas or disaster victims. (7) Your statement that (everything is trending downwards) is true. The trade in cities relies on customers in counties and towns, and the shops in counties and towns rely on customers in rural areas. Now that rural areas are bankrupt, farmers cannot afford to buy goods, and goods in counties and towns are stagnant and cannot be circulated. Cities are also in recession and can only sell at a loss. This downward trend is not a real decrease in the price of goods. It is that farmers' rice is suppressed by the dumping of foreign rice and cannot be sold, resulting in a lack of purchasing power. Therefore, helping rural areas is to help industry and commerce and to bring society to a stable state. If we let it go, farmers will have no way to sell their rice, so they will have nothing to trade, and they will have to stop farming. Taxing foreign rice is a temporary solution, but our association has also requested the abolition of domestic rice taxes and all harsh and new taxes that harm the people as a way to address the root cause. Moreover, rice inspection fees and transit taxes have already been explicitly exempted, and freight rates have also been reduced. The cost of domestic rice has been reduced a lot. If the foreign rice tax is implemented and announced, the intention to indirectly encourage it can be seen. By doing both, the sales of domestic rice will be guaranteed. In short, if Chinese people eat domestic rice, even if the price is higher, the benefits will remain within the country. If Chinese people eat foreign rice, even if the price is lower, the money will flow out of the country. This is the purpose of economic nationalism, and we will not hesitate to use it. We have always admired you as a knowledgeable leader in Lingnan who has studied rural economics. I hope you will not find this long reply tedious. Please review it and provide guidance. Sincerely, The National Federation of Chambers of Commerce of the Republic of China, September 23, 22nd year of the Republic of China.

Reduction of Land Transfer Tax 126

The municipal land value tax has been levied on schedule, and the land transfer tax within the area has also been changed to 2%. It is learned that after the measure was announced by the municipal government, it has been implemented. The land transfer tax was originally levied at 8%, but now it has been changed to 2% due to the collection of land value tax, which is a significant reduction of 60%. Owners in parts of Shanghai South, Zhabei, Yangjing, Pujiang, and Songhuafahua who have land transfers can pay taxes according to the newly set tax rate.

The County Public Funds and Property Office Requests Abolition of Perpetual Tenancy Tax 127

The Shanghai County Public Funds and Property Management Office, etc., sent a telegram to the Executive Yuan and the Ministry of Finance, stating: "On the 8th of this month, Shanghai newspapers reported that the Jiangsu Provincial Government's 594th meeting resolved to levy a perpetual tenancy tax. The public is shocked and says that at a time when the rural economy is heading towards bankruptcy, the provincial government has such a harsh tax for the poor farmers. If this is implemented, the people cannot survive. We should appeal to the central government because the people of Jiangsu are in distress." Yun Shen and others have witnessed the suffering of the people and the strict urging of the elders. We are combining the reasons for the abolition and daring to present them to your Yuan and Ministry. According to the regulations on the promulgation of donation tax regulations, issued by the National Government's Order No. 91 in September of the 20th year of the Republic of China, the establishment of donation taxes must be decided in principle by the Central Political Council and resolved by the Legislative Yuan to be effective. Article 10 of this Perpetual Tenancy Tax Ordinance states that "This Ordinance shall be implemented upon resolution and promulgation by the Jiangsu Provincial Government Committee," which seems to be inconsistent with the procedures stipulated by the government. This is one reason why we must request its abolition. According to this rule, the land transfer tax regulations do not distinguish between the land base and the land interest. The sale deed is taxed at 9%, and the mortgage deed is taxed at 6%. The amount of tax is determined by the distinction between sale and mortgage. The land surface mortgage deed has already been taxed, so the land surface sale deed is another matter. According to the explanation of perpetual tenancy rights, it is the right to use the land permanently, and there is no expiration date for redemption in the contract, which is the same as the current sale deed tax. Now, we want to cleverly avoid the name of the sale deed and implement a double tax system. We believe that the Jiangsu Provincial Government will not be willing to deceive the farmers with profound and distorted interpretations. This is the second reason why we must request its abolition. In recent years, the country has been in trouble, and the landscape is full of scars. We are calling for relief to rural areas. Now, floods and droughts have occurred, and the years are not good. The grain is cheap and hurts farmers. We should consider the foundation of the country, reduce the burden, and relieve the people from weakness. The people of Jiangsu are poor and have exhausted their resources. It is difficult to collect all the regular taxes that have been levied over the years. Now, we are imposing harsh taxes on the dying poor farmers. Even if we strip the marrow and knock the fat, there is no end to the number. This is the third reason why we must request its abolition. Yun Shen and others are heartbroken and have said everything. Although it seems like a warning from a pessimist, it is actually a request for the people. We are telegraphically requesting that your Yuan and Ministry consider the suffering of the people's livelihood, approve the abolition of this ordinance to stabilize agriculture and comfort the people's hearts, and be deeply grateful. Huang Yun Shen, Director of the Shanghai Public Funds and Property Office, Kang Yongnian, Deputy Director, and Wu Shifang, Ding Jicheng, Sun Shiben, Fu Dianying, Xing Zhigang, Wang Chengyao, and others, the six district heads of Shanghai County, respectfully ask for your consideration.

Annual Meeting of the Private Electricity Industry Association to be Held Soon 128

The fifth annual meeting of the National Private Electricity Industry Association is scheduled to be held in Hankou from October 31st to November 6th. The local member, Jiji Water and Electricity Company, is responsible for the reception. The preparatory office for the fifth annual meeting has been organized and is actively preparing. The meeting place has been selected inside the Hankou General Chamber of Commerce, and an electrical exhibition will be held at the same time. Manufacturers from home and abroad will send their products to the exhibition. Individual members will be recruited during the meeting period. Anyone who is related to the electricity industry can join the association and enjoy various benefits. In addition to business meetings, group meetings, tours, and visits, technical and sanitary conferences will also be held, and important papers will be presented. It is reported that in addition to official member representatives, domestic and foreign electrical manufacturers and companies and individuals related to the electricity industry can contact the association's Shanghai communication office at No. 25 Central Road in this city to participate.

Telegrams concerning Cai Yuanpei and others regarding Yuhou 130

Concerning the Yungang Grottoes in Datong, Shanxi Province, the China Archaeological Society's Cai Yuanpei, Ye Gongchuo, Liu Haisu, and others previously reported that the stone carvings were damaged by Commander Zhao Chengshou's troops. The Yungang Villa, located on the east side of the temple, consists of ten rooms and one pavilion. The current construction of the surrounding wall involves quarrying stones from the foot of the mountain opposite the west side of the temple and does not damage the stone carvings. According to Commander Zhao, due to the fame of Yungang, many Chinese and foreign tourists have visited in recent years. The report has already sent a letter requesting correction, etc. After investigation, the situation described is indeed the actual situation, etc. This special telegram is respectfully delivered to Yan Xishan.

Reversal of fortune leads to defeat; Mount Emei faces dire straits again.

Huge sums of money wasted on a futile project; temporary success turns fleeting; The Emei must be towed back to Shanghai by April next year. 131

The Emei steamer of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company ran aground in Fuzhou. Over two months, the company spent a huge sum of eighty to ninety thousand yuan, employing a large number of workers and expending great effort. It was only the day before yesterday that the ship's hull was refloated. The Chongqing branch telegraphed Shanghai, reporting that the salvage was successful and that the ship could be towed back to Shanghai immediately. The company was delighted upon receiving the news and decided to use the ship, after repairs, to launch an express service on the Beijing-Hankou route. This matter was detailed in this newspaper on the 21st of this month. However, yesterday morning, the Chongqing branch sent another urgent telegram stating that the Emei had been salvaged but suddenly encountered receding water, causing the ship's hull to become trapped in a dangerous situation again. This year, it is impossible to salvage. The completed work was defeated in an instant, with huge sums of money wasted. The company was extremely distressed. Upon receiving this alarming news, it was as if struck by lightning. It has now ordered the captain to return quickly and consider other solutions. The situation is reported again as follows:

Sudden Retreat of River Water Causes Ship to Become Trapped Again 132

Emei--Eight weeks of labor wasted,

Nine thousand yuan spent to lift the front half of the ship from the chaotic reefs using the rising water and two small wheels. After repairing the broken hole, it was thought that the salvage was a success. Therefore, the machinery and radio equipment removed from the ship were reinstalled. Shen Jiyun even telegraphed General Manager Liu to say it can be salvaged immediately and come to Shanghai, and the company has prepared for the repair and reconstruction of the Beijing-Hankou new route. Unexpectedly, yesterday morning, the Chongqing branch suddenly sent an urgent telegram stating that the water level of the upper reaches of the Yangtze River had suddenly and drastically receded on the 21st, dropping by more than ten feet compared to a few days ago. This caused the already salvaged Emei steamer to be stranded again on the rocky shore, far from the center of the river, making it impossible to tow it into the water. The effort of nine years was ruined in an instant. The sudden retreat of the river water was unexpected and beyond human control. According to this situation, there is no hope of rising water this year and must wait until the river rises next spring before it can be salvaged again. Huge sums of money are wasted, and efforts are in vain. The unexpected change of events is such that the company has been greatly distressed to receive this telegram. It can only postpone the decided dock repair and the opening of a new route, and meanwhile submit a report to the Ministry for review.

Withdrawal of Crew and Termination of Salvage Operations 133

The re-entrapment of the Emei on the high bank was beyond everyone's expectations. Even the personnel in charge of the matter did not expect it. Although the ship's hull cannot be brought into the river now, the broken holes have already been repaired. It can only wait until April next spring to tow it to Shanghai. The company has telegraphed Deputy Captain Shen Jiyun, who was sent to rescue, ordering him to quickly end the salvage operations and return to Shanghai with Captain Ji Qingrong and the crew. Only a few people will be left on board to maintain the fire and keep watch. Meanwhile, a telegram will be sent from the company to the Ministry, requesting special orders to local military and police and to inform the Naval Department to notify the Yangtze River Fleet to protect the ship at all times, to prevent damage to the ship's machinery and theft of items on board.

Statement from the Municipal Zoo Regarding the Great Bear's Escape 134

And an apology to the startled visitors.

The Municipal Zoo sent a letter to this newspaper yesterday, stating: "Dear Sir, We have read the news in your esteemed newspaper about a large bear escaping from its cage. The editor of the Morning Post also discussed in ('Spare Time Chat') how the great bear escaped. To clarify the facts and dispel doubts, our zoo hereby reports the following: During the period of security for our zoo, it was originally planned to build four sturdy animal houses for lions, tigers, bears, and leopards, and to raise them separately. However, due to budget constraints in the municipal treasury, only two houses were built. In addition to placing the more ferocious lions and tigers in them, a leopard, which is smaller in size but quite ferocious, was kept in the small iron shed that used to house the tigers. As for a large bear, because it was purchased from a performer and is generally docile and without teeth, it was temporarily kept in the small animal house before the large animal houses were added. Unexpectedly, yesterday morning, the bear actually used force to destroy the iron nail caps on the shed door, escaping from the door. The incident was extraordinary, and there was no time to prevent it, causing alarm to the visitors, for which we sincerely apologize. Fortunately, no one was injured, and it was immediately intercepted and returned to the shed. In addition to reporting the facts to the Municipal Education Bureau and requesting that they be forwarded to the Municipal Government to allocate funds to add large animal houses as soon as possible, so as to facilitate relocation and prevent future troubles, we are specifically reporting the facts by letter to clarify the truth and dispel doubts, and to express our apologies to the startled visitors. We respectfully request that you disclose this letter. Yours sincerely, Shanghai Municipal Zoo, September 23rd."

White Russian Merchant Corps' Meat Poisoning Incident Follow-up

Tests Indicate Meat Contained Toxic Bacteria, No Metallic Poisons Found 135

Shanghai Times reports that on Tuesday night, over a hundred of the two hundred members of the White Russian detachment of the Shanghai Merchant Corps stationed in the Tangshan Road camp suffered from abdominal upsets, suspected to be caused by meat poisoning from the lunch. However, all but four people who are still too weak to get up have resumed their regular duties as of yesterday, Thursday. The meat sent to the Public Health Department of the Municipal Council for testing has been found to contain only a trace of toxic bacteria, probably due to contamination of the meat. Friday's Japanese newspapers in Shanghai reported that the illness was caused by members of the Red Party poisoning the lunch. However, after testing by the laboratory, it was found that the meat did not contain any metallic poisons, which was denied yesterday.

Shanghai-Hangzhou Railway to Run Qiantang Tidal Bore Excursion Trains on October 6th, 7th, and 8th 136

The Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway usually runs special trains back and forth for three days during the annual Qiantang Tidal Bore viewing season. Last year, due to the serious national crisis and the Shanghai Incident, the Qiantang Tidal Bore excursion train on this route was suspended. This year, as the Qiantang Tidal Bore viewing season is approaching, the Railway Bureau is specially preparing special trains and arranging for viewing groups and has hired civilian boats to connect and transport passengers. The route has now selected October 6th, 7th, and 8th (i.e., August 17th, 18th, and 19th of the lunar calendar) to run a special Qiantang Tidal Bore excursion train back and forth once a day from Shanghai North Station and Xieqiao. Each time, it will consist of seven first and second-class carriages, one third-class carriage (specially prepared for storing meals and supplies), and one third-class guard car, totaling nine carriages (as one train). It is stipulated that there will be 430 first and second-class seats. The special train timetable is listed below: (October 6th) The special train departs from North Station at 6:50 AM, from Fanwangdu at 7:08 AM, from Xujiahui at 7:16 AM, from Songjiang at 8:05 AM, from Jiaxing at 9:23 AM, and arrives at Xieqiao at 10:12 AM. The special train departs from Xieqiao to return to Shanghai at 3:40 PM and arrives at Shanghai North Station at 7:00 PM. (October 7th) The special train departs from Shanghai North Station at 7:10 AM, from Fanwangdu at 7:17 AM, from Xujiahui at 7:34 AM, from Songjiang at 8:23 AM, from Jiaxing at 9:40 AM, and arrives at Xieqiao at 10:29 AM. The special train departs from Xieqiao to return at 4:05 PM and arrives at Shanghai North Station at 7:25 PM. (October 8th) The special train departs from Shanghai North Station at 7:45 AM, from Fanwangdu at 8:03 AM, from Xujiahui at 8:11 AM, from Songjiang at 8:58 AM, from Jiaxing at 10:14 AM, and arrives at Xieqiao at 11:03 AM. The special train departs from Xieqiao to return at 4:30 PM and arrives at Shanghai North Station at 7:50 PM. After disembarking from the special train at Xieqiao, the passengers will be taken care of by the railway police accompanying the train, and the Railway Bureau will specially prepare 50 civilian boats to connect and transport each boat containing 10 passengers to land outside the East Gate of Haining. The passengers will walk only a short distance (about half a li) to the Tidal Bore viewing arena. Along the way, there will be railway staff and police to take care of and guide them. Upon entering the enclosure and taking their seats, the viewing arena will have tea, refreshments, Chinese and Western cuisine, and the Railway Bureau will send staff to provide hospitality. The four sides of the Tidal Bore viewing arena have been reported by the Railway Bureau to the Zhejiang Provincial Government, which has instructed the Haining County Government to allocate 50 local police officers to cooperate with the railway police to provide careful protection.

Blue-Clad Bandit Sentenced 137

Chen Guofang Sentenced to Three Years in Prison 138

Ge Jingkang, an employee of the Zhenshui Police Department in Zhejiang and a native of Jiaxing, took the Xinjiangtian Wheel from Ningbo to Shanghai at 6:00 AM on the 9th of this month and hired a rickshaw to visit a friend at the Laozha Bridge on Beijing Road. While traveling to the intersection of Zhoushan Road on the Bund in the French Concession, four bandits suddenly blocked the way, showed their guns, and threatened him, robbing him of 45 yuan in cash from the traffic and Siming, etc., in his wallet and fleeing. After the victim reported to the police, the police arrested Chen Guofang, a native of Shaoxing (33 years old, the group all wore blue cloth shirts and trousers and were known as the Blue-Clad Gang), and sent him to the Second Special District Court, which filed a public prosecution on charges of robbery. After the interrogation was concluded, the verdict was announced. Yesterday morning, Judge Wang Gangxu of the Criminal Court sentenced Chen Guofang to three years of imprisonment for being a recidivist of robbery in a group of three or more people. The number of days of pre-trial detention shall be deducted from the imprisonment at a rate of two days for one day of imprisonment.

Yellow Disaster Relief Association's Emergency Relief Personnel Depart Today

Director of Henan Investigation and Relief Office Confirmed as Yang Zigong, Directors of Shandong and Hebei to be Determined Today 157

Mr. Xi Dejiong, director of the disaster relief group of the National Government Yellow River Flood Relief Committee, has been extremely busy planning the distribution of relief funds and recruiting emergency relief personnel since returning to Shanghai on Tuesday after attending the committee's regular meeting in Nanjing. According to Mr. Xi's statement to a Xin Sheng News Agency reporter yesterday, the committee initially intended to establish only Shandong and Henan investigation and relief offices due to the affected areas of Puyang, Dongming, and Changyuan in Hebei Province bordering Shandong and Henan, being far from the provincial capital and having inconvenient transportation. However, due to circumstances and customs, it was deemed inconvenient, and it was decided to establish three offices. As for the candidates for director of the investigation and relief offices, only Henan has been decided, with Mr. Yang Zigong being appointed. Mr. Yang served as the special commissioner for emergency relief in Henan Province and the director of the 18th work relief district during the major flood two years ago and is very familiar with the local situation. The candidates for director of the Shandong and Hebei investigation and relief offices will be determined tomorrow (today). Mr. Yang Zigong, Mr. Gao Dajing, director of the purchasing and transportation office of the group (deputy director of the Lishi Society), and the personnel of the two offices are scheduled to depart tomorrow (today) to implement relief efforts. As for the distribution of relief funds, although regulations have been formulated based on local reports and aerial surveys, funds are being allocated separately for relief. However, it may still be necessary to consider revisions after the investigation personnel conduct on-site investigations and reports. During the conversation, he showed photos of the disaster area taken during the aerial inspection with Mr. Liu Ruiheng and Mr. Zhou Xiangxian last week, where villages were completely submerged in water, with only the tops of trees visible above the water, demonstrating the severity of the disaster.

Jardine Matheson Dispute Resolved, All Workers Resumed Work Yesterday 159

Twenty workers were granted subsidies and dismissed; the rest were reinstated.

According to Dagong News Agency, Jardine Matheson Tug and Lighter Company in the French Concession recently laid off over a hundred people in succession, causing repercussions among all workers. Party and government officials were dispatched to mediate, but it was ineffective, leading to a work slowdown. The day before yesterday morning, more than thirty workers on ten tugs and lighters of the company also joined the work slowdown to show their support. Song Wenkui, the company's Chinese foreman, was deeply concerned that the strike would escalate and become difficult to contain. He invited Mr. Du Yuesheng to mediate. Mr. Du invited Zhu Xuefan and Zhou Xuexiang, members of the General Labor Union, to convene labor and management for mediation the day before yesterday afternoon. As a result, the following resolutions were made: (1) The twenty workers dismissed on August 1st were allowed to be dismissed, and the company would subsidize severance pay. (2) The remaining eighty-plus workers were all allowed to return to work. (3) Wages for the period of the slowdown and the dismissed workers would be paid as usual. Both parties were satisfied and announced the resolution. All the workers boarded the tugs at the Bund yesterday afternoon and returned to work on various lighters as usual, setting off firecrackers to welcome the dismissed workers back to work.

Social Bureau Handles Ash Industry Dispute 160

Reciprocity Contract Should Still Be in Effect

The Mineral Ash Industry Association had a dispute with the Zhichen Brick and Tile Company, a member of the Brick and Tile Industry Association, over the unauthorized transportation of mineral ash to Shanghai, which had lasted for over a month. Although it could have been resolved earlier through repeated mediation by the Municipal Public Security Bureau and the Social Bureau, the company owner, Ling Shumei, raised the issue of the validity of the reciprocity contract, resulting in deep disagreements between the two parties, making it impossible to reach an agreement, and the mediation ultimately broke down. It is now learned that the case has been reviewed and adjudicated by the Social Bureau. The full text of the instructions to both parties is recorded below: (Instructions to the Mineral Ash Industry Association) Noted. It has been verified that the case and the complaint submitted by Zhichen Company to the bureau have been approved and instructed to comply with the settlement reached by the two industries and the reciprocity contract. Please be informed. (Instructions to Ling Shumei, owner of Zhichen Ash Company) Noted. It has been verified that the case and the request from the Mineral Ash Industry Association to correct the company's violation of the settlement and breach of contract have been received. It has also been verified that the dispute between the brick and tile industry and the mineral ash industry was resolved by the Municipal Chamber of Commerce in April of the 20th year, stipulating that the ash suppliers should be responsible for supplying ash to the traders, and the traders should be responsible for selling the products of the ash suppliers. Unless it is necessary due to insufficient supply and demand, the traders must not establish purchasing offices and directly purchase ash themselves. The two industry associations resolved to comply with this agreement and added a reciprocity contract in December of the 21st year. Now that both industry associations exist, the validity of the previous contract naturally continues. How can it be said that the contract has been invalidated? Moreover, the merchant, as one of the representatives for the revision, should not be the first to violate it and directly purchase ash themselves. As for the Mineral Ash Industry Temporary Joint Business Office, which is a trading business, it is even more difficult to simply define it as illegal. You must comply with the settlement reached by the two industries and the reciprocity contract in managing the ash business, and do not cause further incidents and disturbances. Be sure to do so.

Spring and Autumn

Also a First Prize 175

— Lu

Buying airline tickets in the hope of winning the first prize; to get rich, you must win the first prize. It's either nothing, or it's hundreds of thousands of dollars at once. This all relies on luck, without needing any special skills. Therefore, everyone who buys airline tickets hopes to win the first prize.

Amidst the cries of suppressing the communists, there are bounties. Getting the head of so-and-so will reward you with so many tens of thousands of ocean dollars. A head is a head, and a reward is a prize. Head prize money can be simply called the first prize. This kind of first prize requires great skill and great luck. Not everyone can hope for it. Therefore, within the public mind, regarding the same "first prize", the masses only hope to win the first prize of hundreds of thousands of ocean dollars, but don't hope to win the also a first prize of so many tens of thousands of ocean dollars.

When talking about the value of the also a first prize, there is none greater than King Qi's first prize during the Warring States period, and none smaller than Ming Dynasty Grand Secretary Yang Sichang's first prize.

The Strategies of the Warring States has these few words: (Those who can obtain King Qi's head will be granted one thousand yi of gold and be ennobled with ten thousand households.) This is a first prize with both fame and fortune, which of course has richer benefits than the first prize of airline tickets. But who exactly obtained this first prize? The Strategies of the Warring States does not reveal the title of the winner, it's just talk.

In the twelfth year of Ming Chongzhen, Grand Secretary Yang Sichang supervised the army to suppress the bandits and issued a bounty: (斬張戲忠頭賞萬金。) (斬張戲忠頭賞萬金。)(Whoever斩 Zhang Xizhong's head will be rewarded with ten thousand gold.) Zhang Xianzhong knew this and also issued a bounty, mocking Sichang, opening with: (斩杨嗣昌头者赏三钱.) (斩杨嗣昌头者赏三钱。)(Whoever斩杨嗣昌头者赏三钱's head will be rewarded with three qian.)) This is a bit too much of a joke. Above three qian, there is no silver. Of course, it is not three qian of silver, but three wen of copper coins. It is commonly said, "Three wen can buy a stinky fermented eel", so could the head of a grand secretary be equal to a stinky fermented eel? Even if this "three qian" refers to three qian of silver, combining with the modern silver coin, it is only worth four jiao in ocean dollars. Can this be considered a first prize? It can only be considered a small last place.

Recently, I heard that they want to offer a reward to purchase and arrest the traitorous country prime ministers, and I think their also a first prize is probably only worth four mao. Anyway, it can't be done. Opening the price too high increases the value of their first prize, so what is it worth?

On Turtles 176

— Jin Jie

The word "turtle," pronounced "gui" [transliteration omitted], is written as 龜 in ancient texts. Since ancient times, it has been regarded as the leader of shelled insects and is even linked with dragons, phoenixes, and unicorns, collectively known as the "Four Spirits." Although the appearance of a turtle is indeed not very attractive, people often see it as an auspicious creature and believe it to be a long-lived animal, so few people harm it, or at least do not dislike it. I remember reading old novels in my childhood that often contained phrases like: "This person has a round waist, broad shoulders, short neck, and pointed head, exactly matching the turtle form in physiognomy, and will surely achieve great fortune." There was also Mr. Li Guinian, a famous musician of the Tang Dynasty, who specifically used the character "turtle" in his name. This shows that the turtle was indeed highly respected in the past. Even today, the character "turtle" can often be found in Japanese names, such as "Takahashi Kamekichi" and the like.

I don't know when it started, but the character 烏 (wū, crow) was suddenly added to the top of the character "turtle." People wouldn't mention the character "turtle" normally, but when they did, they would shout: "烏龜! (wū guī, turtle, cuckold)" Some of the most impolite people would even say "臭烏龜! (chòu wū guī, stinking turtle/cuckold)" freely, thoroughly insulting the character "turtle" and even using it as a euphemism for those "small husbands who knowingly tolerate their wives' adultery." But this is completely illogical. First, turtles only have "Miss" or "Mrs.," not "Mr.," so they cannot represent males at all. The "Yupian" (玉篇, a Chinese dictionary) clearly states:

"龜. 文也。進也。外骨内肉。天性無雄，以爲雄也。"

("Turtle. Patterned. Advancing. Outer bone, inner flesh. Naturally without males, they consider females as males.")

Therefore, there is also the saying "蛇盤烏龜" (shé pán wū guī, a snake coiled around a turtle), which is a very obvious confirmation. Moreover, the two characters "烏龜" have no origin at all, and "臭烏龜" is even more out of the question! Because we have read the "Erya" (爾雅, a Chinese encyclopedia), in the section on "Interpreting Insects," we have long seen this passage:

"十龜：一神龜，二靈龜，三攝龜，四寳龜，五文龜，六筮龜，七山龜，八澤龜，九水龜，十火龜。"

("Ten Turtles: One, divine turtle; two, spiritual turtle; three, guardian turtle; four, treasure turtle; five, patterned turtle; six, divination turtle; seven, mountain turtle; eight, marsh turtle; nine, water turtle; ten, fire turtle.")

Where is there any mention of "烏龜" (wū guī)?

I believe that the world's reckless trampling of this spiritual creature is also a great sin. The turtle has no personal relationship with me, but the facts cannot be erased, so I wrote this essay about turtles to speak up for them.

Random Thoughts on Cartoons 177

— (Written by Qian Yun) (Drawn by Lian Liang)

It is Precious to Have Sweetness

Whoever is a man walking on the street who doesn't look at women can be crowned a saint; whoever is a woman who speaks without being noticed: this woman has undoubtedly reached old age; a delicate shout and all men obey her, equally undoubtedly knowing that this woman is truly at the height of youthful beauty!

Some are afraid on one hand, and secretly delighted on the other; afraid of the general male making a ruckus, and secretly delighted that they possess an enticing beauty; these types of women love to be accompanied by the same sex when going out: but those with sweetness do the opposite. She can use her sweetness as a nurse, while simultaneously being proud in front of many shady men.

We see it the most in parks; she will use a wide-brimmed hat and a walking stick to scare off the crowd; this is a silent signal that avoids much entanglement; otherwise, men will often pretend to be unintentionally sitting next to a woman's empty seat; so many women do not like walking alone in the park, because Shanghai seems to have too many people using improper means to pick up girls, but conversely, nowadays there are women who have profound knowledge, deliberately leaving an empty seat next to them to lure ignorant men in; naturally this kind of woman has a clear background; it's just that the air in the park is hard to say is fresh!

The Four Northeast Company Commanders 178

— Zhang Henshui

Chapter Fifteen: Guests Leave with Shy Smiles and Gentle Feelings, Old Enemies Arrive, and the Letter Ignites Sadness

Ji Zhi thought: Being a company commander, earning money must be quite a lot, right? It is said that after the salaries are issued, after he pulls out the kickbacks, your business must be better. The shop assistant said: You say being a company commander earns a lot, but that company commander Zhao doesn't even want to do it. I remember this spring, he and a company commander Guan were drinking here, planning to marry a wife. But the family of this bride did not like soldiers, so company commander Zhao became anxious. He said he would quit being a company commander. Company commander Guan persuaded him repeatedly, scolding him, saying that reaching the position of company commander was not easy, and it would not be worth it to lose it for the sake of marrying a wife. When Ji Zhi heard this, he couldn't help but feel a great stimulation in his heart, and even if he wasn't drunk, his face turned red first. He asked: Do you know which family's daughter he was talking about? The shop assistant said: I thought to myself that wanting to resign from his post to marry a wife must mean that this girl is very beautiful. So, I paid attention and listened. It seemed that this girl and company commander Zhao were neighbors. They lived on Haitian Street. Ji Zhi's heart skipped two beats, and he said: Oh! Still neighbors, I wonder if the marriage was successful? The shop assistant said: From the looks of it, the marriage seems to have been successful. Later, company commander Zhao came here a couple of times, and his friends often joked with him, saying that he was going to marry a wife, but he was still doing his job. I don't think there is such a fool in the world who would be willing to lose his job for the sake of a wife. Ji Zhi said: That's not necessarily true? There are plenty of people who lose their jobs for women. There was someone on the road who lost his job out of anger because he couldn't get a wife, not to mention that he was still getting one. As he said this, he laughed loudly, picked up his wine cup, and took a sip of wine. The shop assistant couldn't see through what he meant. What business is it of yours who company commander Zhao marries that you are so anxious? (One nine five)

Soviet Russia's Excavation of Imperial Tombs 179

To alleviate famine, Soviet Russia excavated the imperial tombs of Petrograd. They first opened the tomb of the recent Alexander III, then Alexander I, but the tomb was empty; it is said that Alexander III died in Taganrog, and was later buried in Petrograd, but now it is confirmed that the emperor Alexander lived as a monk in Siberia, ending his days there. Our country also has such mysteries. It is said that Emperor Shizu of the Qing Dynasty broke through the illusions of the world and secretly went to Mount Wutai to become a monk, but because the Qing court deeply concealed the matter, it remains a mystery to this day. According to historical accounts, Emperor Shizu was the first emperor of the Qing Dynasty to enter the Pass, and when he ascended the throne, he was very young. The Empress Dowager ruled the country and had an affair with Dorgon, the uncle of Emperor Shizu, and later formally married him, like the folk custom of "the uncle taking over the sister-in-law." At that time, Emperor Shizu's knowledge had developed, and he harbored hidden pain in his heart, but there was nothing he could do, and he had to formally issue an edict, respectfully inviting his uncle to enter the palace to live with the Empress Dowager, which was extremely scandalous! Furthermore, the matter of failing to take a certain concubine was even more discouraging, so there was a legend that he became a monk. In the past year, a great wave of tomb robbery suddenly arose around Pingjin, and the tombs of great figures of the Ming and Qing dynasties, such as Liu Jin and Dorgon, were successively robbed, and even the Qing imperial tombs were not spared, but the tomb of Emperor Shizu was not robbed. Therefore, some people thought this way: if Emperor Shizu's tomb were excavated, it would be a rare opportunity to dispel the mystery, as long as there was no corpse in the tomb, the story of his becoming a monk would be confirmed. Indeed, this is a rare opportunity, but how can we openly excavate and verify it if the petty thieves have not robbed it? I also have a feeling: great figures of the past were all buried richly after death, which just encouraged theft over the years. After the change of dynasties, they were mostly unable to avoid being exposed and their bones uncovered. Even Empress Lü could not avoid being dug up as a lascivious corpse in times of chaos. It is better to be an ordinary poor person who can sleep peacefully forever. Just like the Russian

imperial tombs, if they were not buried in silver coffins and with treasures, there would not have been the act of excavation. Secondly, foreigners indeed do things in an orderly and methodical manner. The Soviet Russia's excavation of imperial tombs also organized a coffin-opening committee, and the excavation was carried out according to the orders of the chairman of the committee, while our country is just petty thieves robbing at night. This point cannot be compared, but the Soviet Russia's excavation was completely secret. This time, it was a Soviet political detective who leaked the news, which was published in a newspaper in Warsaw, the capital of Poland, and then spread to the world, which is somewhat similar to our country's digging, isn't it? Just kidding!

A Paradise for Children

Choosing a Bride 180

— Yin Yang

Once upon a time, there was a young and strong shepherd who wanted to choose a maiden to be his wife. He knew of three maidens who were equally beautiful, so he had difficulty choosing. Which one should he choose? So he went to ask his mother for guidance, asking her to decide for him. She said: "Prepare a table of food and wine, and invite these three equally beautiful girls to eat. Place some cheese in front of each of their seats, and pay attention to how they eat it, to determine the standard for choosing." The young shepherd obeyed his mother's instructions and prepared a table of food and wine, and placed some cheese on the table. Then he invited the three beautiful girls to eat. The first girl swallowed the cheese together with its rind; the second girl hastily and carelessly cut off the rind of the cheese before eating it, but she cut it too quickly, so that a lot of the delicious cheese was lost together with the rind; the third girl slowly and carefully cut off the rind of the cheese before eating it, and the amount of rind she cut off was neither too much nor too little. The young shepherd saw these three different ways of eating and went to tell his mother. She said: !

"You can choose the third girl to be your wife"; because she knew from the way she ate cheese that the third girl was a meticulous, gentle, shrewd, and capable person. Sure enough, after they got married, they lived a very happy life.

The Twins' Birthday 181

— Yin Feng

Jake and Bailey are twins, identical in appearance and figure. In a certain week, they will hold a celebration for their sixth birthday, so they plan to save some money to buy birthday gifts for each other. Now Jake knows a man named Mr. Smith who has an adorable puppy for sale, something Bailey would definitely like. Bailey also knows about this puppy and thinks what a great birthday gift it would be to buy it for Jake.

So one morning, Bailey went to Mr. Smith's house and said:

"Mr. Smith, how much do you want for your puppy?"

"You want to buy the puppy, great," Mr. Smith said, "It's very cheap, it only costs five shillings." But Bailey only had four shillings and eleven pence on him, not enough for five shillings, so Mr. Smith said: "It doesn't matter, since your birthday is on Friday, I'll keep the puppy and not sell it to anyone else. On Friday evening, you can bring five shillings and take the puppy home."

Unexpectedly, on Wednesday, Jake brought five shillings to Mr. Smith's house to buy the puppy. Mr. Smith was not at home, Mrs. Smith went to the door and took one look, and she thought he was Bailey without a doubt. She took his money and gave him the puppy. Bailey really went to Mr. Smith's house again on Thursday. When Mr. Smith saw that the puppy was gone, he knew it had already been sold to someone else.

"I'm very sorry," he said, "Would you like to buy a bunny instead?" So Bailey bought a bunny for Jake. On the morning of their birthday, the twins looked out the window as soon as they got out of bed. Children! What do you think they saw? Let me tell you. They saw two birthday gifts running around on the grass, looking very happy. They had never seen anything so friendly in their lives. Of course, Bailey was very surprised to see this puppy, and Jake also loved this bunny very much. In the past, these twins always divided everything equally, but now they agreed that the puppy and the bunny should belong to both of them. From then on, they did everything well.

(Children! The two names "shilling" and "penny" in this story should be explained. These are the names of British coins, just like our country has coin names such as "silver dollar," "dime," and "steel yuan." They are not decimal, twelve pence is one shilling, just like twelve feet is one inch. The dimes commonly used in the Shanghai market now are also not decimal, one silver dollar can be exchanged for more than twelve dimes.)

All Sports Yesterday Suspended Due to Rain; All-Around Competition Concludes This Afternoon

Chinese Football Club Old Members Registration

Starts immediately 190

This year's Chinese Football Club competition is scheduled to be held at the Promotion Association field as usual. However, due to the conflict with the two major citywide and national games in the recent months of September and October, the field, players, referees, etc., have all been affected. Therefore, the competition date will inevitably be delayed. The Promotion Association secretariat is actively preparing and has decided to start accepting registrations from old members immediately, with a deadline of September 30th.

All old members of the club who wish to continue to participate in this year's competition, or who do not wish to participate this year for various reasons but wish to retain their membership, should have their team managers provide their contact information and formally register or notify the Promotion Association by letter. Those who fail to register or notify by the deadline will be considered as not participating in the competition or withdrawing their membership. All teams are requested to implement this immediately to avoid delays.

As for the recruitment of new members this year, it will depend on the number of teams joining that were old members, and a decision will be made later. If recruitment is necessary in the future, the registration period will begin in early October. Please pay attention.

National Games Awards: Letters Sent to Various Organizations Requesting Donations in Cash 191

(Nanjing, 23rd) The National Games Organizing Committee, previously considering that the awards made by various organizations were inconvenient to distribute, sent letters requesting that they be changed to donations in cash. Except for the Central Party Headquarters, which has already made and donated fifteen large and small silver cups, and the National Government, which has ordered the Mint to manufacture a large number of awards, the cash donations received from other organizations include: the Executive Yuan, 200 yuan; the Ministry of Transportation, 400 yuan; the Central Military Academy and the Military Senate, 200 yuan each; the Judicial Yuan, the National Central University, and the Audit Department, 100 yuan each. Together with donations from other organizations, the total has reached several thousand yuan.

Hebei Province Representatives Selected for National Games 204

Scheduled to Go to Beijing on the 5th of Next Month

(Special Dispatch from Tianjin) The National Games are scheduled to be held in the capital on Double Tenth Day. The preliminary selection meeting for Hebei Province's participation was opened on the 18th, and the preliminary rounds for various events began on the 14th. The finals for each event were completed on the 19th. Due to the small number of participants in this preliminary and final round, everyone lacked a competitive spirit, so the performances were not very exciting. In particular, most of the track and field events did not meet the standard. Only Dong Jingchun in the 200-meter breaststroke broke the national record with a time of 3 minutes and 16.5 seconds. (According to the 17th North China Games, the national record holder for the 200-meter breaststroke was Huang Maoyuan with a time of 3 minutes and 28 seconds). This was barely satisfactory. As for women's swimming, Hebei Province has never had anyone participate, but this time Ms. Li Luanding showed her skills, which can also be regarded as unprecedented. Yesterday (the 20th) at 2:00 PM, the selection committee was convened in the Department of Education, and the representative team was selected. The selection was completed at 6:30 PM. All elected representatives should report within today (the 21st) and tomorrow to fill out commitment forms. Those who fail to report within the deadline will be replaced by alternates. American and French International Professional Tennis Tournament: Cochet and Tilden Each Win a Set 227

Cochet (France) Wins Against Pounce (USA) in a Thrilling 3-2 Match 228

Tilden (USA) Wins Against Paria (France) in Straight Sets of Three 229

(Havas, Paris, 22nd) American and French professional tennis players began their matches today at the Roland Garros tennis court, with an audience of approximately 4,000 people. The French players were Cochet and Paria, while the American players were Tilden and Pounce. The format of the competition is similar to the Davis Cup, with two singles matches on the first day, one doubles match on the second day, and two singles matches on the final day.

The first match today was between Cochet and Pounce. Pounce boldly adopted an aggressive strategy, his forehand shots accurate and swift, forcing Cochet to play defensively. Pounce even took the lead at 4-3 at one point, but Cochet then displayed his best tennis of the era, leveling the score at 4-4. He then won two consecutive games to take the first set 6-4. The skill displayed by both players in the second set was truly a sight to behold. Cochet frequently went to the net for volleys, allowing him to gain a 5-4 advantage. However, Pounce won three consecutive games, winning the set 7-5. In the third set, both Cochet and Pounce hit the ball with proper form. Cochet ultimately won 6-4. In the fourth set, Pounce launched a fierce attack, causing Cochet to run around the court, unable to keep up. Pounce was flawless, winning the set 6-0. In the fifth set, Pounce ultimately struggled to cope with fatigue. When Cochet took a 3-0 lead, Pounce attempted a counterattack, but Cochet's forehand and backhand shots landed perfectly, interspersed with excellent drop shots, allowing him to gain a significant 5-1 advantage. Although Pounce managed to win back two games, making it 5-3, Cochet ultimately won 6-3. The final score was 6-4, 5-7, 6-4, 0-6, 6-3.

The second match was between Tilden and Paria. At the beginning, the game was fast-paced. Tilden won the first set 6-3. Then, the game was suspended due to rain. After an hour, the rain stopped, but the court was still damp. Tilden took advantage of the situation, frequently attacking the corners, causing Paria to exhaust himself. Thus, Tilden won the second set 6-3. In the final set, Tilden's technique was superb, his shots landing accurately, ultimately winning 6-2. At the end of the first day, both France and America had each won a set.
