Severe Punishment for Forging Diplomas 232

The Ministry of Education has already issued an interpretation regarding whether those who present forged graduation diplomas from various provinces and cities should be punished. Now, because there are further requests for interpretation, it has been reported to the Judicial Yuan for interpretation. The general idea is that although it is understandable that students forge graduation diplomas in the hope of furthering their education, the diplomas bear official seals, and forging seals is a crime, and should be punished with several months of imprisonment. It is heard that the Ministry of Education has interpreted according to the Yuan's order and will soon issue a circular to the education departments and bureaus of various provinces and cities and the universities and colleges directly under its jurisdiction for compliance.

Local News

Formal Publication of the Index of the Siku Quanshu Reprinted by Photography 233

Recommendations from the Index Compilation Committee: Three Matters

180 Types of Books Selected for Printing

Since the Ministry of Education announced its plan to reprint the Siku Quanshu by photography, scholars from the north and south have given it extreme support. However, the method of selection requires specialized research and joint discussion. In order to gather opinions from all sides, the Ministry of Education appointed Li Shengduo, Dong Kang, Fu Zengxiang, Chen Yuan, Yuan Tongli, Xu Naichang, Liu Hanyi, Zhang Zongxiang, Xu Hongbao, Fu Sinian, Liu Yiwei, Zhang Yuanji, Ma Heng, Zhao Wanli, and Gu Jiegang on August 15th as members of the Index Compilation Committee. They were assigned to specially review the (Draft Index of Unpublished Books) compiled by the Central Library, and it was decided that one month would be for discussion and two months for compilation. Each committee member corresponded back and forth, and the list of books to be selected for printing has been compiled. The committee members selected 142 types of books from the 366 types of books in the draft index of the Central Library, and added 38 types of books that were omitted from the index. All books with good editions that could be substituted were eliminated for separate printing. The selection was extremely careful. Yesterday, a letter was jointly sent to Minister Wang, explaining the reasons and attaching three methods, which are very insightful. The index was released simultaneously in Beijing, Ping, and Shanghai yesterday. The letter from the committee members to the Minister of Education and the attached methods are recorded below:

Letter to Minister of Education 234

To Minister Xue Ting,

Previously, we received your letter of appointment and attached a copy of the index of unpublished books of the Siku Quanshu. We are grateful for the commission to review it. Now, after repeated discussions and detailed examination by our colleagues, we have selected 143 types of books from the original index, and added 37 types, totaling more than 90,000 leaves. We have also formulated three methods, which are listed below. We respectfully await your inspection and hope that you will make a quick decision and complete the project soon, which we will all be grateful for.

Sincerely,

Three Attached Methods 235

(1) The Library Edition and Good Editions Should Be Equally Emphasized. Among the books recorded in the Siku Quanshu, there are many that have not been printed since the Qing Dynasty. However, they can generally be divided into two categories. The first category is books compiled from the Yongle Encyclopedia that have no other editions to replace them, or those collected by the Siku that originated from old Song and Yuan editions, or those that are not far from the era and are extremely rare. We have selected 143 types of books from the current draft index of unpublished books and added 37 types, tentatively named the Siku Orphaned Edition Series. The second category is Song, Yuan, and Ming printed editions or manuscript editions that are better than the Library Edition. These will be compiled into a separate index, named the Siku Rare Edition Series. The former, after being reviewed and approved by the ministry, will still be handled by the Central Library and the Commercial Press according to the contract, in order to facilitate early circulation. For the latter, we propose that the ministry order the Peking Library to formulate a plan and gradually prepare for it. Our colleagues will certainly do their best to contribute to this great undertaking. (1) Collation Notes and Index Should Be Printed and Distributed Simultaneously. In addition to the Wen Yuan Ge, there are other editions of the Siku Quanshu stored in the country, such as the Wen Jin Ge. Although they come from the same source, there are often differences in the text. After the previous books are printed, we propose that the ministry order the Central Library to compare them and write collation notes to avoid regrets. In addition, most of the books in the Library Edition do not have indexes at the beginning of each volume, which should also be added and distributed simultaneously to facilitate reading. (1) Each Book in the Series Should Be Printed and Distributed Separately. The series contains many works written before the Song and Yuan dynasties, many of which are urgently needed by scholars for research and examination. However, the volumes are vast and not within the reach of poor scholars. We propose that the Commercial Press be ordered to print more separate editions at low prices to make them easily available to poor scholars, and that ancient books can be widely disseminated, so as not to fail the ministry's elegant intention to promote scholarship.

Types of Orphaned Editions 236

The published list of books includes 35 types of classics, 15 types of history, 24 types of philosophy, and 106 types of collections, totaling 180 types.

Restructuring of the Shen Bao Correspondence School of Journalism 238

Since its opening in April of this year, the Shen Bao Correspondence School of Journalism has received enthusiastic enrollment. Recently, due to the original organization being insufficient to cope with the demand, a special commissioner has been appointed to preside over school affairs starting in September. Experts in journalism in China have also been hired to share teaching responsibilities, and the school address has been moved from the Continental Commercial Building back to this building. The internal organization has been completely revamped. The lectures that were not fully issued previously will be fully issued according to the regulations starting in October. It is estimated that there will be more than 100,000 words of various lectures each month, not including exercises. Student homework will be personally graded by the professors of each course, without being tired of asking for details. If students can completely complete each subject within one year, it is equivalent to the courses taught in a two-year vocational school, that is, they can be fully trained to become a very useful journalism talent. After another six months or a year of practical training, their ability can be responsible for reporters in major newspapers. The restructuring of the school has been completed, and the third enrollment of new students is also being continued at the same time. Anyone who has graduated from high school or has equivalent qualifications can apply for admission at any time. After passing a written examination, classes will begin. There are a total of 18 types of lectures in the school, divided into required and elective courses. The required courses are: 1. Chinese, 2. Practical Journalism, 3. Printing Knowledge, 4. Newspaper Organization and Management, 5. Advertising, 6. Newspaper Promotion, 7. Current Affairs Research, 8. Correspondence Practice, 9. Publication Law, 10. Reporter Knowledge, ten types. The elective courses are: 1. Selected Readings of English Newspapers (and English News Production), 2. Introduction to Journalism, 3. Foreign Journalism, 4. Domestic Journalism, 5. Commentary Writing, 6. News Storage, 7. Prose Research, 8. Photography, eight types. Each course is a practical and useful knowledge, and the knowledge and skills that researchers of journalism should have are also included. The study period is one year, and the tuition fee, including the lecture fee and postage, is only 15 yuan per year. The low tuition fee is unmatched by any other correspondence school. The purpose of the school is to cultivate domestic journalism talents. Those in the country who cannot afford to enter a formal vocational university but are interested in journalism should not miss this opportunity. Details will be sent upon request.

Free Talk

Inquiring About Impressions 239

— Tao Zhui

Since the May Fourth Movement, it seems that Chinese people have developed a new habit: whenever a foreign celebrity or rich person arrives, they like to inquire about their impression of China.

When Russell came to China to lecture, radical youths held meetings and banquets to welcome him and inquire about his impressions. Russell said, "(You treat me so well that it's not good to say bad things.)" The radical youths were indignant, thinking he was slippery. When George Bernard Shaw traveled around China, reporters in Shanghai gathered to interview him and also inquired about his impressions. Shaw said, "(My opinions have nothing to do with you. If I were a warrior who killed a hundred thousand people, you would respect my opinions.)" Revolutionaries and non-revolutionaries were all indignant, thinking he was harsh.

This time, it was Prince Carl of Sweden who came to Shanghai. The reporter also published his impressions: "(…Wherever he went, he was warmly received by local officials and people, and he was extremely grateful and happy. This tour has brought him a very good impression of the government and people of your country, which will never be erased.)" This is the most stable, I think, and will not cause any trouble.

In fact, Russell and Shaw were not considered slippery and harsh. If there were a foreigner who, when asked about his impressions, first asked, "(What is your own impression of your own China?)" That would be a truly difficult article to write.

We were born and raised in China, so if we have feelings, they cannot be considered impressions); but opinions are fine; but how can opinions be expressed? Saying that we are like fish in muddy water, living in a confused and inexplicable way, doesn't sound like an opinion. Saying that China is very good is probably also difficult. This is what patriots mournfully call "(losing national self-confidence)," but it really seems to be lost. Asking everyone about their impressions is just like seeking omens and divination, because of the suspicion in their own hearts.

Within us, there are certainly those who express opinions. What we often see are those without power or courage, who have not "(killed a hundred thousand people)," but rather call themselves "(common people)," so their opinions are not "(respected)," that is, they are "(unrelated)" to everyone. As for the bigwigs who have power and influence, perhaps they were very radical when they were out of power, but now, they are silent 丨 China "(treats me so well that it's not good to say bad things.)" Looking at the current situation of the gentlemen who rose from the (New Tide Society) who welcomed Russell at the time and were indignant at his answer, it is really felt that Russell was not slippery, but a prophetic satirist, who said ten years later's thoughts in advance.

This is my impression, and it can be considered a mock answer, copied from the mouths of foreigners.

Peasant Poet 240

— He Ru

Whether it's old poets or new poets, there is still a lack of peasant poets in the modern Chinese literary world. This is a fact. The collapse of the rural economy and the unbearable suffering of peasants have been felt by economists, politicians, and revolutionaries. Have sensitive poets not felt it? The land tax in Sichuan has been pre-collected for who knows how many years of the Republic of China. There are always hundreds of miscellaneous taxes, but unfortunately there are no detailed investigations or statistics. The special dispatch from Nanchang in the Shen Bao on the 20th said, "(The Economic Association investigated the land tax surcharges in 33 counties in eastern, western, and northern Jiangxi, reaching more than 90 types. In Yushan, each stone of rice is taxed more than 20 yuan. A certain weekly magazine reported that Guangfeng taxed up to 60 yuan per mu, and the rest also reached several times the regular tax, and the district, bao, and jia temporary apportionments are extorted anytime and anywhere, and cannot be investigated.)" Another dispatch said, "(The early rice in the Fu River has fallen to 1.8 yuan per dan. Because of the bao, jia, road construction, and bandit suppression donations and taxes, farmers want to sell cheaply even if they are starving, but no one buys. The rural area has become an Avici Hell.)" Is this Avici Hell limited to a corner of Jiangxi? Is there a paradise anywhere in the entire China? We do not expect great poets like Du Fu and Bai Juyi, who can have a little leisure and occasionally write a few poems about social problems, as long as there are small poets like Yu Fen and Nie Yizhong who are not valued by society, that would be enough for our literary world to boast about.

Speaking of Nie Yizhong, perhaps everyone is very familiar with him. "(Hoeing millet under the noonday sun, sweat drips onto the soil below. Who knows that every grain in the dish is hard-earned?)" This poem of compassion for farmers, which is said to be by Li Shen, is said to be by Nie Yizhong. We have read it in elementary school textbooks since we were young. There is also "(Selling new silk in February, selling new grain in May. Healing the sore in front of the eyes, cutting out the flesh in the heart.)" This poem, titled "Lamenting the Farming Family," is also the most widely recited work of Nie.

As for Yu Fen, he was not very famous at the time, and no one has praised him since. In fact, when it comes to peasant poets of the Tang Dynasty, he is perhaps more authentic than Nie Yizhong. Unfortunately, very few of their poems have been handed down, with only one volume recorded in the Complete Tang Poems. Like Nie Yizhong, Yu Fen was also stuck in the lower ranks. It is not difficult to explain why they sympathized with the farmers who had no one to complain to. Yu Fen's "Thoughts at Dawn in a Mountain Village":

Opening the door to see the millet, the neighbor lives by the water's edge. Today, the waves of the southern stream, last night's rain in western Sichuan. A shepherd boy wears a short raincoat, a waist flute awaits at the misty islet. Not asking the people by the water, he rides his cow and goes to the mountain. This kind of sketch of pastoral life is not as (rigid) as Tao Yuanming or Chu Guangyi. But his description of the suffering of peasants, such as saying "(The one plowing on the ridge, plants with his hand but his belly is hungry. The girl throwing the shuttle under the window, weaves with her hand but has no clothes on her body.)" (Hard Work Chant) "(The one who dwells in a rock cave, calls a dwelling his property. Although he is covered with a towel, he is not as good as a dog in a noble family.)" These are not what poets of the Tao, Xie, Wang, and Meng families, and even Chu Guangyi, who sing about pastoral landscapes, would deign to stain their noble poetic pens with.

We know that the famous warlord wars of the Tang Dynasty are referred to in historical books as the Disaster of the Fiefdoms. This kind of war fell on the heads of the peasants, while the warlords and bureaucrats took the opportunity to get promoted and make a fortune to marry concubines. Yu Fen, who can be called a peasant poet, unveiled the inside story of the war in his poem "Ancient Warfare," but it was only a minority of people who were satisfying their desires for money and beauty. The soldiers in this kind of war only got "(Red flesh, painful golden wounds, others become Wei Huo)" As for his saying "(A song of the ancient Liangzhou, six relatives live on blood. I advise you to have long eyebrows, learn to sing to feed your relatives.)" (Weaving Silk Song) Those who get promoted through nepotism have had enough!

In today's China, there are no thorough national heroes. If you want to be a national poet, you are suffering from a lack of great themes. It is not easy to deceive people by creating illusions and allegories. If there is a poet who is willing to use his noble poetic pen to describe the lowly peasants, there are many moving themes for you to choose from. The peasants will not reject you. Is there really no poet like Nie Yizhong or Yu Fen?

A Drama Without Clowns 241

—

I have seen very few Chinese spoken dramas, probably because the impression I got from some domestic films I watched before was so bad that I dared not go to see spoken dramas again. It is said that the stage is even more difficult than the silver screen.

However, I finally saw a few spoken dramas, and sure enough, the impression I got was even worse. What disappointed me the most was that there was not much difference from the so-called "civilized dramas." Even when performing a great tragedy, a few clowns would be added for no reason, turning the plot into a farce, and in the end, the audience would just laugh and leave. Of course, the fun was quite interesting, but the tricks of the Great World were even more interesting than this. Recently, I accidentally read a string of newspapers and suddenly found some eye-catching large characters in the advertisement column, "Roar, China!" This made me quite surprised. Anyone who cares a little about modern drama knows that this is a famous drama composed of new consciousness and new art. Naturally, this opportunity should not be missed. However, checking the small print next to it, I was disappointed again: it turned out that it was not a movie, but a spoken drama staged by Chinese people themselves, which I dared not watch again.

On the evening of September 16th, while strolling around Baixianqiao, I was suddenly dragged into the Golden Grand Theater by a friend wearing a badge with the word "Cadre" on his chest. Well, although I am not enthusiastic, I don't have to be as stubborn as Zilu and not understand worldly affairs.

This was the first day of the public performance, but the audience was not enthusiastic, but there was no need to be surprised. Just looking at the name, you could understand that there were no kisses or women's thighs. Although the Chinese are a country of etiquette, they seem to like kissing and women's thighs even more than foreigners.

The white lights went out, and the colored lights came on.

Merchant ships, warships, crosses, and gallows; fat-headed foreign compradors, laboring workers... appeared before my eyes.

On the stage, there was the victorious cheers of the oppressors and the tragic cries of the oppressed, but under the stage, the unconscious noise suddenly turned into dead silence.

"Roar, China!"

This slogan spread from the stage, and a thunderous echo suddenly broke out under the stage. The audience was awakened by this thunder and rushed out of the theater like a tide.

The cool night breeze calmed my tense emotions, and I felt that my heart was satisfied and full. I saw the excited faces of every audience member, which made me even happier.

Of course, such a meaningful spoken drama cannot yet be popularized among the masses, but being able to move a part of the audience is ultimately meaningful. Although the Drama Association's performance this time still has many shortcomings in terms of technique, the fact that it has this power to move proves that there are also many successes. And the clown who won the audience's laughter did not appear in this performance, which also proves that Chinese spoken drama is progressing.

Random Notes from a Mountain Dwelling by A Ying 242

—

(7) Killing People and Eating People

Someone wrote a novel that promotes the national spirit, called "The Battle of the National Gate." The most proud part of his writing, which is also the most nationalistic, is killing people. He himself gets drunk, raises his knife and splits open people's skulls, letting the white brain matter gush out from the top of their heads: he writes it as vividly as a dragon and a tiger, which makes one's heart palpitate. Because of reading this novel, I thought of an event recorded in "Haiguoting's Anecdotes":

During the Sui Dynasty, Ma Shumou and Zhu Can steamed children as food; during the Tang Dynasty, Gao Zan steamed his concubine and ate her. Yan Zhen and Dugu Zhuang both loved to eat human flesh, but they all made it into minced meat before eating. There were no raw eaters. During the Liang Dynasty, Yang Daosheng saw an old subordinate being tied up, drew his sword, gouged out his eyes, and swallowed them. During the Song Dynasty, Wang Yansheng captured some Hu people, held a wine banquet, tore off their ears with his hands, chewed on them for a long time, and then slowly drank a cup of wine. The captives were covered in blood and cried out in pain, but Wang Yansheng talked and laughed as if nothing had happened. He ate hundreds of people in total, which was worse than tigers and wolves.

Reading "The Battle of the National Gate" can make you tremble with excitement, while reading this record will make it even harder for you to retract your tongue. Wang Yansheng's spirit and the heroic act of splitting open skulls are both admirable. It is a pity that in 1927, in XX, we don't know who was the person who stripped women's clothes, executed them by shooting, and then inserted a kaleidoscope into the dead person's vagina and set it on fire to achieve pleasure. Otherwise, it can truly be said that these three are equal in their brutality. Writing here, I also remembered a similar record in "Shao Shi's Anecdotes": Emperor Wu of Han used Du Zhou as the chief justice of the imperial prison, arresting as many as sixty to seventy thousand people in a row. The number of officials who increased the charges reached more than one hundred thousand. During the reign of Empress Wu of Tang, when interrogating exiles, Wan Guojun killed three hundred people in one day, Liu Guangye killed nine hundred people, and Wang Deshou killed seven hundred people.

Killing people is truly an everyday occurrence in China, and it is the same in both ancient and modern times. What is especially commendable is that not only must the killing be plentiful, but it must also be artistic, with all kinds of postures and methods. China can truly be called a nation of murderers.

Illiteracy Eradication Center by Constantin Fedin, translated by Lin Yizhi 243

—

The garden, the old rusty chimney, the gravel, the accumulated water, the children by the water's edge, and the cat walking behind the children. Every day when I go out of the house, I see these things through the window, and I often think in my heart that I should go around to the back of the side house in the garden to see what's going on there. But why go? What to do? If someone suddenly asks, "What are you doing here?" Wouldn't that be embarrassing? Therefore, I have never been to this garden even once, and even this house will be moved soon. This is the fate of most adults: the door of the house is open to the street for adults. The garden is just the world of children.

The life of Ma Wufutelovna, a female teacher at the Illiteracy Eradication Center, is the life of a wanderer. She has lived in many houses; but for some reason, her thoughts still live in an unfinished house, and she has always been drifting when there was no garden in that house.

○ ○ ○ ○ ○

The small wooden house was very quiet, with two dim lamps lit; the small wooden house, which was usually so dirty, was illuminated very cleanly by the two lamps, and the shadows were beautifully reflected on the wall. The air in the room was warm and quiet, shrouded in Ding Jia's head, and the warmth and quiet made him drowsy, but he couldn't sleep. "(Eighteen plus six,)" Ding Jia wanted to drive away the Sandman, so he deliberately read aloud: "(Eighteen plus six equals twenty-four.)"

It was time to go to the Illiteracy Eradication Center for class immediately. But he hadn't memorized his homework well, and Ding Jia thought of the stern face of the female teacher Ma Wufutelovna, and he was a little worried.

"Why can't I always remember it?" he thought in his heart, and put on his clothes.

He was late for class.

"You are always late," Ma Wufutelovna complained to him: "Sit down quickly, don't disturb others."

The earthworker Ke Bidejin, about fifty-five years old, with a cunning and kind face, was holding a newspaper and reading slowly:

"Now we should first pay attention to the iron smelting furnace factory. In order to start the high-speed construction of this factory, we must make special efforts; the Party and social groups must..."

"That's right, you read it well," Ma Wufutelovna interrupted Ke Bidejin: "You have reviewed it at home, and you can understand it as soon as you hear it. It is most important to review at home. Just taking classes here, just taking classes here, there is no hope. If you don't review at home, you won't make progress."

She called Ding Jia's name:

"You read this book." She took out a small book from a full little leather bag and handed it to Ding Jia, she said: "These words are very clear."

"Can't I read the newspaper?" Ding Jia asked timidly.

A Review of the American Cotton Market for the Past Week 258

A telegram from New York on the 22nd reported on the cotton market for the past week, stating that the rise in the cotton market last week was due to the excitement of currency inflation and the weakness of the gold standard. However, after the authorities expressed opposition to inflation, there was a large amount of long liquidation. At the same time, prices fell, short covering was very strong, and fellow traders also made considerable purchases. Furthermore, there were rumors that the Soviet Union would have large cotton loans and France might purchase huge quantities of raw cotton. China also increased spot orders when prices fell. Domestic cotton mills also showed increased demand after the cotton cargo transactions of the previous week. Operators have slightly changed their estimates of this year's cotton harvest due to abnormal weather in the middle of the month. Generally speaking, everything depends on developments in Washington and further progress in industrial recovery.

Starch Rises Quickly and Steadily 261

After the market opened yesterday morning, starch prices showed an initial flat and then rising trend. Chicago and Canada also continued to rise by about four or five cents, so the market atmosphere was still flat when prices opened. This month still opened at 1.7 dimes, but due to outside speculation, there was gradual short covering. Even the chips of the factories also had short covering, which caused the sentiment inside and outside the industry to be affected. Bidding prices for all months rose step by step. By the time the market closed, the total increase was one, two, or three cents. When the market opened in the afternoon, it was quite calm at first. However, due to rumors in the market that the situation between Japan and Russia was tightening and that the situation in the Far East might change in the future, the factories again frantically covered this month, frequently and actively absorbing them regardless of the market price. As a result, outside speculation also followed closely, resulting in an abnormal situation and a rapid rise. However, distant factories still released them, which was similar to the situation at the end of the previous month. It is not known how things will change in the future. As a result, September and October each rose by four and four cents, November rose by three cents and seven and a half mils, December rose by three cents and two and a half mils, January rose by two cents, and February rose by two cents and seven and a half mils.

The failure of overseas silk telegraphs to turn the market atmosphere around makes it very depressed. Although European and American hoarders in Shanghai are trying to support the market, they are relentlessly suppressing prices. Chinese silk merchants are unwilling to sell at a loss, so the silk market is stagnant and the future is pessimistic.

This newspaper has repeatedly received letters from readers asking how to read economic or commercial news. The reporter has often been unable to answer in detail because the issue involves too much. Recently, financial expert Professor Yang Yinpu has spent more than two years creating a book titled (How to Read Economic News), with a total of 200,000 words. It not only solves the reader's problem of (how to read economic news), but also provides detailed general knowledge of finance, market conditions, and various commodity market conditions. It is truly the best reference book for merchants in all industries. The book is published by Liming Bookstore on Sima Road in Shanghai and is priced at 1.8 yuan. The reporter has obtained the consent of the bookstore to offer a 25% discount on the list price to readers of this newspaper who cut out this introduction and go to the bookstore to purchase the book.

An Astonishing Message 271

On the recent solemn commemoration of the second anniversary (1918), in addition to publishing memorial texts in various forms, newspapers also carried an astonishing message: H.G. Wells, the British literary figure and author of the renowned (The Outline of History), predicted that major upheavals would occur in Asia's Far East within ten years, and that all of China would suffer immense devastation. The four hundred-odd provinces of China would descend into a state of extreme chaos...

According to our observations, the reaction of the general newspaper-reading public to this message falls into one of the following two categories: (1) those who habitually pay no attention to the domestic and international situation take this prediction to be, at best, similar to the words of a (fortune-telling blind man). They believe it is not to be fully trusted and should be listened to while observing the aftermath. (2) Friends with a fair understanding of the domestic and international situation believe that this prediction cannot be compared to the kind of predictions made by astronomers or geologists about changes to the sun in one hundred thousand or fifty thousand years, or the eventual split of the earth. The latter are merely temporary conclusions drawn from academic research, whereas Mr. Wells' prediction is entirely based on the current international situation. If the direction cannot be practically changed, and things continue to worsen day by day, then this kind of speculation is a necessary consequence, and someone would have said it long ago even without Mr. Wells' prediction. The difference is that no one before has been as categorical and vividly calculated as this literary figure, predicting what will happen in 1935, and what will happen from 1936 to 1938. Perhaps this is the difference between ordinary speculation and prophecy!

Seeing how countries today are desperately reorganizing their national defense and expanding their armaments, and looking back at our own domestic political disunity and the daily weakening of our national productive capacity, we firmly believe that it is very difficult to avoid the literary figure's prediction by chance. So, should we sit and wait for death, or should we immediately begin to prepare, each doing our best to contribute our abilities and intelligence to the work of fighting and resisting? But what is the actual situation? The reporter has roughly described it in the previous issue of (A Week Worse Than the Last - The Second Anniversary) rambling talk, so there is no need to repeat it. In short, the government authorities lack the appearance of striving for self-improvement, and the masses are like a heap of loose sand, full of a mentality of complacency and selfishness. Someone said: (The day the Second World War breaks out will be the day our Chinese nation begins its revival!) Even if this abstract, unfounded theory has some basis, we should also know that while a world of great chaos may provide an opportunity for oppressed nations to revive, it also carries the risk of causing an old nation to perish! The key is to see whether this old nation has made preparations for revival on the eve of the impending outbreak of the World War.

Mr. Xu Shanxiang, who recently returned from the United States, said in a speech on the American Revival Plan at the International Problems Research Association: (When the situation is critical, the American people can grant power to the government to act expediently, and can sacrifice political prejudices to support it unanimously. This spirit is essential for a republic, but we Chinese completely lack it. Although five million square miles of territory have been lost and the great enemy is at hand, we are still fighting internally every day, fearing only that the country will not perish.) Finally, Mr. Xu warned the people even more loudly, saying: (Within a few years, China will have a very great depression, ten times worse than today. The value of foreign goods imported last year reached over 89.1 million gold units, while the quantity of native goods exported was only worth over 41.9 million gold units, with a trade deficit of about 47.19 million gold units, equivalent to 870 million national currency. Calculated on the basis of 400 million people, each person bears about 2.2 yuan. Given China's current situation, the majority of people are so poor that they have no place to stand. How can they have the strength to take out two yuan per person and send it to foreign countries? It is inevitable that the nation will go bankrupt!) Then, after bankruptcy, will we be slaughtered by others, or will we rise up quickly to survive and prepare to resist? This is up to our own decision.

Thinking of relying on others and hoping for others' help is all wishful thinking!

The Hope of Hopeless Life

Chen Zixin, A Small Clerk in a Company 272

When I entered this big company among hundreds of competitors, how happy I was! Friends and relatives all came to congratulate me, praising me for having real talent and learning, and saying that my future would surely be full of hope. So I prepared my best effort and came to serve in this big company full of hope.

On the first day I entered, the general manager lectured us (eight people were admitted) and said: (You are all handsome young people with rich knowledge, and this company will regard you as pillars. Now, this company is like a dark room, and you are all electric lights. As long as you can work hard to make this company shine, I will definitely not treat you badly.) Ah, what a warm and sincere lecture that gave people hope! So we began to bury ourselves in hard work.

After working hard for a month, it was payday. Unexpectedly, I only received half of the expected salary. While I was wondering, the general manager called us together for a lecture. He said to us:

(You must be a little disappointed today, and I apologize to you very much for this. Your salaries were not determined by me personally, but were decided at a meeting. Several directors believe that you have all received secondary education or higher, and must be indifferent to material gain. Moreover, you are all very young in reality, and I suppose you do not have much of a burden... Shanghai is a place where people from all walks of life gather, and the good and the bad are mixed. Young people have unsettled blood and qi, and if they have extra money on hand, they will often go astray... So, on the one hand, it is also for your sake. Fortunately, there will be a performance review at the end of the year. As long as you work hard, a raise and promotion are very easy, and I will definitely not treat you badly!)

Alas, (indifferent to material gain), (no great burden), (extra money on hand, often go astray), after listening respectfully, we had to endure and withdraw. But when I thought of what he said: (At the end of the year, as long as you work hard, a raise and promotion are very easy...) So we were filled with hope again and continued to work hard.

The end of the year came, and the New Year arrived. Everyone went happily to receive their own salaries in January, but unexpectedly, the salary was still the old amount, with not a single cent added!

We couldn't bear it any longer, and the eight of us went to see the general manager together. Before we could open our mouths, the general manager said first: (I already know why you've come, but the company didn't make much money last year, so I'm going to have to ask you to wait a while. Because if I give you a raise now, others will be afraid to follow suit, and it will affect the overall situation, making things

On Four Amateur Artists 274

Chen Wenzi (1)... (1)

Yan Chonglou, from Shaanxi, 25 years old, an employee of Wuzhou Pharmacy on Henan Road.

Every night, around eight o'clock, he returns home from the office, his spirit still so cheerful.

He is a young man who loves poetry, literature, and music very much.

Every night, without interruption, beautiful and magnificent melodies leap from the strings of his Wanhualin lute, so graceful and melodious. The telephone pole outside the window seems moved as well, its "eyes" twinkling with a serene light. The rickshaw puller on the street corner falls asleep on the footboard, forgetting his day's hard life. Music that harmonizes life's bitterness!

Then he begins to recite a poem along with the melody: (Sleep, grotesque world. Let the people in distress exhale a sigh of relief.)

(2)... (2)

Yang Zhongpo, from Shaoxing, also 25 years old, an employee of Aihua Pharmaceutical Society on Shandong Road.

Late at night, in the bedroom, all his other colleagues are sound asleep, snoring away, but he alone is quietly contemplating under the flickering candlelight, pondering, pondering. The sharp tip of his pencil dances lightly and heavily, densely and sparsely on the sixty-pound drawing paper, sketching out the outlines of various figures.

Elegant, harmonious colors, skilled brushstrokes, clean outlines. Although his artistic skills have not yet matured, the path to success has already unfolded before him.

Indeed, he has never attended an art school, nor has he received guidance from anyone with artistic experience. He relies entirely on his own research, practice, and references. He never loses heart for a moment.

Now, his works have been welcomed by many newspapers and publications.

(3)... (3)

Zhou Tianlai, originally from Anhui, a pawnshop appraiser at Yuanlai Pawnshop on Fuzhou Road in this city.

Whenever he has a break from work, he fumbles with his large format camera. Beautiful spring suburbs, summer evenings by the river, autumn parks, winter villages, he finds natural beauty there, treating it as the subject of his photography.

One Saturday afternoon, he quickly finished the things that should be done in the shop and came to ask me to go to the art school to photograph the nude human body. He was really obsessed with art. It took quite a while to pass two big homes… The woman who was to be the model was already impatient, and the atmosphere was awkward. How the chest should be positioned... After much careful lens adjustment and lighting, he finally took a picture. On the way back, he smiled and said: (This time the results will be great!) However, most of his monthly income is spent on this sort of thing. Yet he says: (Sacrificing money for art is nothing to be stingy about.)

(4)... (4)

Mu Yilong, an 18-year-old young man, a local, works in the stock exchange.

His only treasure is that set of tools, large, small, flat, and angled knives.

The gentlemen in the exchange often say this with admiration. Yet, he is still tirelessly seeking artistic refinement. He says: (There is no end to art.)

Business Common Sense: Preparations for Starting a New Store by Zheng Lixuan 276

People who work in the business world generally have a hope: that after working hard for others for several years as a clerk, they will save up some capital through frugality, and in the future, they can start anew and establish their own business (as for whether this hope can become a reality, that is naturally another matter).

Therefore, in this context, the necessary preparations when starting a new store should be something everyone is happy to hear about!

The preparations for starting a new store, such as finding a location, installing equipment, stocking goods, and hiring employees, are things that anyone with a little business experience can probably understand. However, in addition to these extremely common preparations, there are a few points that are extremely important and that all entrepreneurs should know. I will select the essentials and describe them below:

(1) Registration: In recent years, various industries in Shanghai have organizations called trade associations. These organizations have good and close relationships with the same industry. When a store is first established, it should first register with the association, which will definitely help with the progress of the business. Secondly, the Shanghai Social Bureau has a commercial and industrial registration office, and you should also go there to register before the store is established to obtain legal status.

(2) Insurance: Once the registration procedures are complete, when you are starting to do things, you should pre-allocate the total amount of capital. For example, if the total amount of capital is 5,000 yuan, use 1,000 yuan for (goodwill), store base equipment, decoration, etc., use 3,000 yuan for goods, and 1,000 yuan for working capital. Then, this store should be worth at least 4,000 yuan besides cash. Once you have an approximate amount, then find a stable and reliable insurance company to take out fire insurance. Because disasters are unpredictable, fire insurance costs are limited, but the assets are already protected, so you won't suffer from unexpected disasters.

(3) Extraneous expenses: All the necessary procedures have been completed. At this time, there is still one very important thing that should be noted: In all levels of society in Shanghai, there is a special class called (loafers). These people specialize in finding a living by extortion and fraud. They have organizations and (colors). Naturally, when a new store is established and opened, you should try to contact them in advance and give them a good impression, so as to avoid being subjected to all kinds of unavoidable and vicious slanders when opening.

Timely Article: Reflections on the September 18th Incident and National Heroes 277

Ms. Bi Xiang: More than two years have passed since the September 18th Incident. Although it has now been declared over with the authorities enduring the pain, the loss of life and property to the people is unprecedented in our country. The resources of the four northeastern provinces have already fallen entirely into the hands of Japanese imperialism; even the losses in Shanghai during the war were equally huge. However, under the influence of narrow patriotism and patriotic movements at the time, several so-called (national heroes) who shook the world were created, which is truly a fortunate thing for our nation!

However, what exactly did these national heroes accomplish in the anti-Japanese movement? This is worth studying.

Originally, after non-resistance, the outbreak of resistance was an inevitable result, and it was bound to be initiated from among the lower-ranking officers and soldiers. However, when contact between the two sides had already begun, their superiors, these national heroes who did not want to resist, were still forcing them to remain calm, telling them to strictly abide by the orders of their superiors. It was not until later, when the war became a situation where they were riding a tiger, coupled with the fact that those who did not resist were deeply resented by the masses, and most hoped that those who resisted would step forward, that these national heroes transformed themselves and took advantage of the trend to engage in so-called resistance, using this opportunity to create their own position and at the same time win praise. As a result, the sacrificers were some brave lower-ranking officers and soldiers, while those who reaped the benefits were still these national heroes. What is most incomprehensible is that some national heroes once surrendered to Japanese imperialism midway, some national heroes were busy with (internal pacification), and some national heroes were also key figures in the signing of the Shanghai truce agreement. These were the greatest tasks they completed in the anti-Japanese movement.

In this anti-Japanese and anti-imperialist upsurge, since the national heroes have shown themselves to be so incompetent, and their actions are suspicious in every way, then why are there still people holding on to idol worship, expressing warm welcomes to these national heroes, and hoping that they can show great power? However, we must know that this is just a portion of the backward petty bourgeoisie succumbing to the impulse of narrow national consciousness, and the majority of the working masses will never believe in these heroes, because they deeply know that the anti-Japanese and anti-imperialist movement cannot be borne by a few people, let alone implemented by one or two national heroes. If we want to know what national heroes can actually do, it is that they are similarly obstructing the progress of the anti-Japanese and anti-imperialist movement. Conversely, only the working masses who are the most oppressed and exploited are the main force in the anti-Japanese and anti-imperialist movement, and only they can firmly shoulder this major task; otherwise, China will never be liberated from the oppression and exploitation of Japanese imperialism and all other imperialisms.

A Small Social Model: The Blacks of China - Lu Han 278

Steamboat fire hold, in the steamboat's fire hold. In front is the hot furnace fire, behind is the sooty coal pile, only cramped, stuffy, smoky, roasting: enclosing the entire fire hold. The heat, ten times worse than the hot wind blowing from India in early summer, is true, even dogs can't live there, but we have to live in it. Who wants to? But we have to in order to eat, even if we don't want to!

Each person manages three furnaces, nine furnace openings, using long furnace rake iron, coal shovel, coal hook, shoveling, digging, excavating the black coal, one shovel, two shovels sent to the hot furnace, while cleaning out the coal slag and sending it to the salt field... Doing like this, from the first furnace opening all the way to the ninth, over and over again, endlessly. Truly, you can't even rest for a second, otherwise the furnace fire will slow down, the (water ting) (steam) will be light, and the (Namowan)'s ham leg will be coming to your butt again.

Working hours are really long! The first watch is four o'clock, the second watch is another four o'clock, eight hours a day is called (on watch), in addition, you have to do two hours of coal slag cleaning work. Ah! Ten hours a day living in that stuffy fire hold. Fortunately, there is a bit of vitality, that is, the fresh wind blowing from the canvas wind funnel on the side of the chimney top, it is still the life-saving medicine for us stokers (firemen).

Are we people? It really doesn't seem like it, our entire bodies are being braised all day by that coal dust and heat, braised to be dozens of times blacker than a turtle, simply like the blacks of South Africa.

Because we are breathing in fire and coal dust, black dust, accumulated over a long time, therefore every stoker becomes a coughing-up-blood internal injury (people often call it tuberculosis) ghost. At the same time, because of the uneasy life and the heart-wrenching flames of the hot fire, they go crazy, become mentally deranged, to the point of jumping into the sea, lodging in the bellies of fish... it also happens often, how many times it happens every year among the more than 800,000 sailors is unknown!

The work must be done, and wages must be paid. Stoker's wages are generally twenty-five yuan (for those on foreign routes) and twenty-three yuan (for those on coastal routes), and inland river boats have as little as fifteen yuan or twelve yuan. Regardless of the whys and wherefores, (Shi Sha) when you get off the boat to work, the first thing is to deduct all of your first month's wages, then deduct two to six or seven yuan per month, in addition to expenses such as accommodation commission, likin, tea money, teacher money, student money, debt, interest payment, telephone fee (accommodation use), god's birthday fee, gifts...etc., a large number of expenses must be paid out of these twenty-odd yuan wages. As for parents, wives and children longing for your support, alas! That only gets, only gets (unfilial) and (uncompassionate).

Then, in the absence of a way, you want to find a way to find some (extra money), (selling yellow croaker) (smuggling passengers)? Can't, only (Namowan) can do that. Want to do some tax evasion? That also can't, the Customs is tight, the inspection is strict, bringing ten pounds of salt from Hong Kong, or shipping some copper coins from Shanghai to Guangdong, will also be subject to strict searches or investigation. No way, (extra money) is really not an economic outlet!

Outlying Postal Agency: Student-ified Workers and School-ified Factories by Zhang Taoran 279

Hunan Baoqing Correspondence

Speaking of the Hunan XXX Textile Factory, almost all Hunanese know about it, because it is the largest textile factory in XXX. It started as a privately-run enterprise, but later the manager and factory director deducted workers' wages, not paying workers what they deserved for more than a year, which caused a worker strike. The capitalists took the opportunity to shut down the factory. It wasn't until six or seven years ago that XXX took it over, directly subordinate to the XXX authority. The factory is now divided into two departments: a yarn factory and a cloth factory. The yarn factory is divided into more than ten departments, including cotton carding, cotton cleaning, cotton blending, combing, drawing, roving, spinning, reeling, packing, and cotton picking. The cloth factory is divided into eight or nine departments, including warp yarn, weft yarn, sizing, weft yarn, heddling, weaving, and cloth folding. The factory building is made of cement and reinforced steel, and the roof is sawtooth-shaped lead. Inside, the air is constantly flying with cotton fibers like falling snow, so most of the workers suffer from chronic tuberculosis. If you are new to the factory, you will definitely feel that your breathing is suffocated by the cotton fibers.

There are currently around 4,000 workers in the factory, of which 800 to 900 are women. Most of the male workers have a junior high school education, but there are also those with a senior high school education, and even those with a university education. Most of the female workers also have a junior high school education. There is also a labor union in the factory, but the workers do not trust it very much, because whenever there is a conflict between the workers and the capitalists, the people in the labor union often say to the workers: Now is a time of national crisis, labor and capital should cooperate to increase production; workers must not take illegal actions, if there is anything, they should wait for the union to resolve it, etc. Thus, each request is just (waited for) like that. The union also nominally publishes a bulletin board, but in fact the bulletin board is done by the workers themselves, published every three days, the content is mostly focused on politics and worker life, and literary works are also published in each issue.

Workers work ten hours a day, divided into day and night shifts. The highest wage is six jiao, and the lowest is four jiao five fen. Supervisors and foremen are very brutal towards the workers; physical abuse is even commonplace for child laborers. If workers do not perform well in terms of production, they will be fined, scolded, or given a demerit; after three demerits, they will be fired. However, if female workers show some affection towards the supervisors and foremen, they are less likely to suffer these misfortunes.

After the workers get off work, some go to the club to play. There, various entertainment items, such as chess, musical instruments, etc., and various sports equipment, such as football, basketball, table tennis, etc., are available. Some go to the dormitory to study on their own. Some go to the after-school tutoring school established by the factory. The school has about 1,000 students, divided into five levels according to the depth of the workers' knowledge. Classes are held in day and night shifts. Each class is two hours long. The students themselves organized an autonomous association and also compiled a bulletin board, which is published daily. In addition, the school authorities also published a weekly newspaper, which is co-edited by teachers and students. The factory has worker dormitories, specially prepared for single workers to live in, men and women are separated, and no accommodation fee is charged. There is a public dining hall for eating, and the food cost is about five yuan per person per month, and men and women are also separated.

Based on the above, we can know that the lives of the workers in this factory are generally not bad. This is partly because the cost of living in the interior is lower, and partly because the workers in the factory already have a considerable degree of solidarity. After the September 18th Incident, they showed their own strength. They established an anti-Japanese association, organized propaganda teams, speaking teams, and fundraising teams to carry out activities everywhere. They also organized a drama club to perform anti-Japanese and anti-imperialist plays.

Origin of the Amateur Mailbox 280

Previously, this position in the publication published (Shop Assistant Communication). It was added by this newspaper on its 60th anniversary, in view of the fact that most shop clerks and apprentices in this city have difficulties and suffer from not having the opportunity to learn from each other. Its target audience was originally limited to shop clerks and apprentices; but in addition to shop clerks and apprentices, even just in this city, there are many people who have this need. Thank you for not abandoning us, they have all sent letters to communicate. At first, we were very strict with this target audience; so that many valuable questions had to be cut off; later, on the one hand, because the questions specific to shop clerks and apprentices were very monotonous; at the same time, on the other hand, we felt that there was no reason to reject communications from readers other than shop clerks; so we gradually relaxed this target audience. Recently, the communications we have published have come from workers, from the education sector, and also from the administrative sector. In practice, it has very naturally changed from (Shop Assistant Communication) to (Amateur Mailbox). Now, in order to match the name with the reality, we have directly and straightforwardly renamed it (Amateur Mailbox). Based on past experience, we know that in addition to letters that raise practical questions about a certain event, some letters only express personal opinions on a certain issue or describe the situation in a certain scene. From now on, for letters that raise practical questions, the editor will reply to the best of their ability, and those that are universal and that the general public is eager to know will be published in this column, while the rest will be replied to directly by this column (please make your address clear in your letters). As for letters expressing opinions, those that have considerable value will be selected and published directly in this column without adding notes. Readers are welcome to discuss, hoping to establish a common belief in society. As for texts describing the current situation, except for a few extremely reasonable and extremely unreasonable ones that will be published in installments for all parties to learn from; the rest will not be answered. In short, the work from now on will focus on replies; and the published texts, except for those related to the public interest, will prefer quality over quantity.

Biography of a Famous Person: Mussolini's Childhood (Part 2) by Ge Tianwen 282

From the ages of six to nine, when Mussolini was studying in elementary school, he was a restless and extremely annoying child. He loved to quarrel and fight with other children, and making trouble was practically his daily routine. As a result, his scalp was often scratched open by sharp stones, and his face was often covered with crisscrossing claw marks. This wasn't the biggest problem; what was most annoying was his pair of small hands, which often stole other people's things. Once, he stole a lark from a hunter (used as bait), and when the hunter discovered it, he chased after him closely. Mussolini climbed over a small hill in one breath, ran across a meadow, and swam across a small river blocking his way. Even though the situation was so critical, he still held onto the lark in his hand, refusing to let go. As for stealing other people's bayberries and grapes, it was such a common occurrence that it was countless.

Mussolini was already twelve years old. Although he was still mischievous and disliked studying as always, his parents were worried about the misfortune of his impending school dropout. Life was so difficult that even the bare minimum of living could not be sustained. Forced by circumstances, Mrs. Mussolini had no choice but to compose a letter to the governor of the welfare province, pleading in earnest and pitiful words, requesting permission to grant her a small subsidy so that her son would not drop out of school. The letter said:

(I remember you once visited our school and gave us compliments. You said that I, who have served for a long time, should be entitled to a subsidy from the Minister of Education; your words are those of a benevolent man, please do not let them pass. Originally, I was extremely unwilling to make such a fuss easily, but this year the local market situation has become too bad. Not only is the harvest poor, but the grape seeds have also rotted. My family is in this situation, and it is foreseeable that my twelve-year-old child, who is studying well at the Royal Public School of Welfare Popoli, will not be able to continue; according to the teachers:

He has great prospects. If you could give me a small allowance, or teach me a way to prevent my son from dropping out of school, I would never forget it!)

These words, when heard by the great men, were naturally no different from the east wind passing the ear, and not worthy of their concern. So, in the end, with the governor's reply of (ignored) and (disapproved), it was inserted into the governor's office's files, never to see the light of day again. But this unfortunate answer did not discourage her; she only worked even harder to encourage her son.

In desperation, Mussolini's mother had to force her son to receive religious education, and decided to send him to the Salesian boarding school to study. Mrs. Mussolini felt that this was the best possible solution, as she was a devoutly religious woman; but Mussolini's father, Alessandro, strongly opposed it, because this gentleman deeply resented all the inequalities in society and became a powerful world revolutionary. In his revolutionary eyes, religion was nothing more than an anesthetic, a tool for rulers to subdue the people, so naturally he was very opposed to it. How could he be willing to send his son to enjoy this kind of anesthetic? However, in the end, he yielded to his wife's will. This was inevitable, as he had no way to get his son out of the circle of religious education, unless he dropped out of school altogether.

In the week before Mussolini entered school, his behavior was even worse than before. He knew that boarding school life was no different from a prisoner's imprisonment, so he simply took advantage of this time before he was imprisoned to have a good time. So he ran wildly in the streets, wandered in the fields, and jumped around in the forests and vineyards, like an untamed wild horse.

All the preparations for school were soon completed, which seemed like a disaster to Mussolini. On the one hand, he was reluctant to separate from his beloved parents and his three-year-old sister, Edvige, and seven-year-old brother, Arnaldo; on the other hand, he couldn't bear to part with his beloved canary, which was placed in a clean cage and hung on the window of his small room. As he packed his bags and prepared to leave, his eyes were filled with tears. He slowly climbed into the mule cart, and turned back to urge his mother to take good care of the bird.

The tired mule pulled the dilapidated mule cart forward on the sloping and uneven dirt road, his father acting as the driver. He sat in the cart, his mind in turmoil, and his homesickness rose and fell like the swallows flying in front of the cart. In the evening, the cart arrived at the gate of the Facaga Salesian School. The father and son silently got out of the cart, and after knocking on the door for a while, a lame and old priest who was also the principal greeted them. In the dim light, the principal touched the child's head and said with a smile: (What a lively child!) End. Mussolini's father settled everything with the principal, then kissed his son and left the school.
